The Four Caliphs and the Ten Promised Paradise
Author affirms caliphate of four imams and testifies paradise for ten.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the caliphate of the four caliphs and the testimony of paradise for the ten Companions.

Core Idea
Allah guided the four caliphs and promised paradise to ten Companions.

Imam al-Ash'ari states the Sunni creed regarding the rightly guided caliphs and the ten who were promised paradise. This passage clarifies the proper stance towards the Companions and their disputes. It establishes the basis for loyalty to all Companions and the superiority of the four caliphs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style and the sequential listing.
2
Identify the four caliphs
The passage lists three caliphs explicitly after mentioning Abu Bakr on the previous page. Note the order and the remark about Uthman's killers.
The author emphasizes that Uthman was killed unjustly.
3
Understand 'caliphate of prophethood'
Reflect on the phrase 'خلافة النبوة' – what does it mean for the caliphate to follow the prophetic model? This is a key Sunni doctrine.
4
Grasp the stance on the ten and all Companions
The author testifies paradise for the ten, shows loyalty to all Companions, and refrains from discussing their disputes. This is the balanced Sunni approach.
The word 'نكف' means we refrain or withhold.
5
Affirm the superiority of the four
The passage concludes that the four imams are the most virtuous, none equals them. This is a clear statement of their rank.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه . ثم عثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنه ، وإن الذين قتلوه قتلوه ظلماً وعدواناً . ثم علي بن أبي طالب رضي الله عنه . فهؤلاء الأئمة بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وخلافتهم خلافة النبوة . ونشهد بالجنة للعشرة الذين شهد لهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بها ، ونتولی سائر أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ونكف عما شجر بينهم . وندين الله بأن الأئمة الأربعة خلفاء راشدون مهديون فضلاء لا يوازيهم في الفضل وغيرهم .
Then Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him. Then Uthman ibn Affan, may Allah be pleased with him, and indeed those who killed him killed him with injustice and transgression. Then Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him. These are the imams after the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, and their caliphate is the caliphate of prophethood. And we testify of Paradise for the ten whom the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, testified of Paradise for them, and we are loyal to all the Companions of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, and we refrain from what occurred among them. And we make it our religion before Allah that the four imams are rightly guided, divinely guided, excellent caliphs, none equals them in virtue.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement affirming the succession and virtue of the Companions. It begins by listing the four caliphs in order: Abu Bakr (implied from previous page), Umar, Uthman, and Ali. It emphasizes that Uthman was killed unjustly. It then declares that their caliphate was that of prophethood (following the prophetic model). Then it testifies that the ten Companions promised Paradise by the Prophet are indeed in Paradise, and it adopts a stance of loyalty to all Companions while refraining from delving into their disputes. Finally, it affirms that the four rightly guided caliphs are superior and none equals them in virtue.

Key Terms
الأئمة الأربعة
خلافة النبوة
العشرة المبشرون بالجنة
أصحاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Sunni doctrine involves cursing or hating some Companions or that the caliphs were not divinely guided.
Correction: The author affirms loyalty to all Companions, refrains from their disputes, and asserts that the four caliphs are rightly guided and none equals them in virtue.

Checkpoint
What does Imam al-Ash'ari say about those who killed Uthman?
A) They were justified in their actions.
B) They killed him with injustice and transgression.
C) He does not comment on them.
D) They were Companions who disagreed.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari affirms the caliphate of the four rightly guided caliphs, testifies paradise for the ten, and directs loyalty to all Companions while refraining from their disputes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you truly free from any pride or prejudice towards any of the Companions? The author commands 'we refrain from what occurred among them'. Is there a conflict between Companions that you secretly side with one party over another? Repent and purify your heart today.
?
The author testifies that the ten Companions are in Paradise solely on the Prophet's word. Do you fully accept every explicit statement of the Prophet without hesitation? Is there any hadith you doubt or explain away to suit your desires? Commit to submitting completely to his testimony.
?
The caliphate of the four is called 'the caliphate of prophethood'. In your own life, do you follow leaders who embody prophetic guidance? More importantly, does your own leadership (in your family, community, or workplace) reflect the prophetic model? If not, what step will you take today to align with it?

Rulers and Rebellion: Sunni Political Doctrine
Imam Ash'ari mandates prayer for rulers and forbids armed rebellion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical Sunni position on praying for rulers, acknowledging their imamate, and forbidding armed rebellion.

Core Idea
Sunni doctrine requires patience with rulers and forbids revolt, even against unjust ones.

In this passage from Al-Ibanah, Imam Ash'ari articulates a core Sunni political principle: loyalty to the Muslim community's leadership does not mean blind obedience, but it does mean refraining from armed insurrection. The author establishes both a positive duty—to pray for rulers—and a negative prohibition—to avoid rebellion, especially during times of civil strife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully, then the literal translation. Note the two distinct parts: the positive command and the negative prohibition.
2
Identify the three components
The author lists three obligations: supplication for rulers, acknowledging their imamate, and deeming rebellion misguided when rulers deviate. Find each one.
Also note the second part: renouncing rebellion by sword and refraining from fitnah.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this position was important in Imam Ash'ari's time and how it distinguishes Sunnism from other groups.
This guards against the misunderstanding that Sunni doctrine accepts tyranny unconditionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونرى الدعاء لأئمة المسلمين بالصلاح والإقرار بإمامتهم وتضليل من رأى الخروج عليهم إذا ظهر منهم ترك الاستقامة. وندين بإنكار الخروج بالسيف وترك القتال في الفتنة.
And we hold [the duty of] supplication for the Muslim rulers for their uprightness, and acknowledging their imamate, and [we hold] the misguidance of those who deem it permissible to rebel against them when they show deviation from rectitude. And we make it our religion to renounce rebellion by the sword and to refrain from fighting during civil strife (fitnah).
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage addresses political doctrine: Sunnis are obligated to pray for rulers, recognize their authority, and consider rebellion against them (khuruj) as misguided even if they are unjust, as long as they are Muslims. They must refrain from armed rebellion and avoid participating in fitnah (civil war). This is based on the principle of obedience to rulers except in clear disbelief.

Key Terms
الخروج على الأئمة
الفتنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sunni Islam requires unconditional obedience to any ruler, no matter how unjust.
Correction: Sunni doctrine does not mandate approval of injustice, but it forbids armed rebellion because it leads to greater harm (fitnah). Believers are to pray for rulers and remain patient.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ash'ari, what is the ruling on those who deem rebellion permissible against a ruler who deviates from righteousness?
A) They are following a valid interpretation
B) They are misguided
C) They are excused for their intention
D) They are to be executed

Key Takeaway
Sunni political doctrine mandates prayer and patience toward rulers while prohibiting armed rebellion even against unjust rulers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness injustice from those in authority, is your first impulse to turn to social media complaints or to sincere supplication for their guidance? What does that reveal about your trust in Allah's command?
?
Are there any 'swords' you have drawn—in your speech, your thoughts, or your online arguments—against rulers or leaders? Will you renounce them today, even if you feel justified?
?
This teaching demands submission to a difficult command: no rebellion, even against oppressive rulers. Is there a part of your heart that resists this? What would it cost you to fully accept it, and are you willing to pay that price?

Refutation of Deviant Sects on Three Core Beliefs
Imam Ash'ari enumerates the three denials of the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three specific beliefs that the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya denied according to Imam Ash'ari, and the foundational evidence from narrations and consensus that he cites.

Core Idea
Three beliefs denied by deviant sects are upheld by Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus.

Imam Ash'ari opens this chapter by exposing the errors of two deviant groups: the Mu'tazila and the Qadariyya. He first criticizes their method of interpreting the Quran based on personal opinion without prophetic or scholarly authority. Then he pinpoints three key doctrines they rejected—the vision of Allah, the intercession of the Prophet, and the punishment of the grave—all of which are firmly established by transmitted narrations and the consensus of the early Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Imam Ash'ari structures his criticism: first the method, then the three denials.
2
Identify the three denials
List the three specific beliefs that the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya denied: vision of Allah, intercession, and grave punishment.
Each denial is stated in the passage with a brief proof.
3
Analyze the evidence cited
For each denial, note the evidence: for vision, mutawatir narrations; for intercession, narrations from early Muslims; for grave punishment, consensus of Companions and Followers.
4
Reflect on the importance of transmitted knowledge
Imam Ash'ari emphasizes that these beliefs are not based on opinion but on transmitted reports and consensus. Consider why this method is foundational in Sunni Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما بعد : فإن كثيراً من الزائغين عن الحق من المعتزلة وأهل القدر مالت بهم أهواؤهم إلى تقليد رؤسائهم ومـن مـضـى مـن أسلافهم، فتأولوا القرآن على آرائهم تأويلاً لم يُنزل به الله سلطاناً، ولا أوضح به برهاناً، ولا نقلوه عن رسولِ رب العالمين، ولا عن السلف المتقدمين -فخالفوا روايات الصحابة - رضي الله عنهم - عن نبي الله صلوات الله عليه وسلامه في رؤية الله عز وجل بالأبصار، وقد جاءت في ذلك الروايات من الجهات المختلفات، وتواترت بها الآثار، وتتابعت بها الأخبار . وأنكروا شفاعة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم للمذنبين، وردوا الروايات في ذلك عن السلف المتقدمين . وجحدوا عذاب القبر، وأن الكفار في قبورهم يعذبون، وقد أجمع على ذلك الصحابة والتابعون - رضي الله عنهم أجمعين -
As for after: Indeed many of those who deviate from the truth from the Mu'tazila and the People of Qadr, their desires led them to imitate their leaders and those who passed before them from their predecessors. So they interpreted the Quran according to their own opinions, an interpretation for which Allah sent down no authority, nor did He clarify any proof, nor did they transmit it from the Messenger of the Lord of the Worlds, nor from the early predecessors. So they contradicted the narrations of the Companions - may Allah be pleased with them - from the Prophet of Allah, may Allah's blessings and peace be upon him, concerning the vision of Allah Almighty with the eyes. And indeed narrations have come regarding that from various directions, and the reports have been mutawatir (massively transmitted), and the reports have followed in succession. And they denied the intercession of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, for the sinners, and rejected the narrations regarding that from the early predecessors. And they denied the punishment of the grave, and that the disbelievers are punished in their graves, while the Companions and the Followers - may Allah be pleased with all of them - have agreed upon that.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the first chapter. It begins with a general criticism of the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya, accusing them of following their whims and taqlid of their leaders, leading them to interpret the Quran based on their own opinions without divine authority or transmitted proof. Then it specifies three denials: 1) The vision of Allah (ru'ya) in the afterlife, which is proven by numerous mutawatir narrations from the Companions. 2) The intercession (shafa'a) of the Prophet for major sinners, which they rejected despite reports from the early Muslims. 3) The punishment of the grave (adhab al-qabr), which they denied, but which the Companions and Followers unanimously agreed upon. The passage sets up the refutation that follows.

Key Terms
الزائغين
المعتزلة
أهل القدر
رؤية الله بالأبصار
شفاعة رسول الله
عذاب القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya had valid reasons for denying these beliefs, or that Imam Ash'ari is just making accusations without evidence.
Correction: Imam Ash'ari points to transmitted evidence: mutawatir narrations for vision, earlier narrations for intercession, and consensus for grave punishment. These beliefs are not based on opinion but on established sources.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following did the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya deny?
A) The vision of Allah and intercession only
B) The punishment of the grave only
C) All three: vision of Allah, intercession, and punishment of the grave
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila and Qadariyya denied three core Sunni beliefs — vision of Allah, intercession, and grave punishment — but these are firmly established by narrations and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran or learn about Islam, do you ever find yourself ignoring clear texts because they conflict with your desires or the opinions of people you admire? How would Imam Ash'ari's warning about following personal opinion apply to your own learning?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed to be rational, yet they denied things that are solidly transmitted. Have you ever rejected a teaching because it seemed irrational to you, without checking if it is authentically from the Prophet and the Companions?
?
If someone you respect—a scholar, a leader, or a friend—denied a belief like the punishment of the grave, would you have the courage to stand with the consensus of the Companions and Followers, even if it means disagreeing with that person? What would you say to them based on this lesson?

Al-Ash'ari's Accusation Against the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya
Al-Ash'ari introduces the chapter by accusing the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya of denying the vision due to taqlid and contradictory interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's critique that the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya denied the vision of Allah due to blind imitation of leaders and rejection of mutawatir reports.

Core Idea
Denial of Allah's vision stems from blind imitation, not from evidence.

In this opening of the chapter, al-Ash'ari sets the tone for his refutation of the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya. He does not start with a theological proof but with a methodological critique: these groups have abandoned the proper sources of knowledge—the Qur'an interpreted with authority and the mutawatir narrations—and instead followed their leaders. This lesson examines that critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the key accusations and the contrast between taqlid and mutawatir narrations.
The passage is densely packed with technical terms.
2
Identify the two sects
Note that al-Ash'ari mentions both al-Mu'tazila and ahl al-Qadr (Qadariyya). He treats them together as deviant groups.
3
Analyze the reason for deviation
Al-Ash'ari says their desires led them to follow their leaders (taqlid) and interpret the Qur'an without divine authority or proof.
The phrase 'fi al-nuzila' means they claimed an interpretation without sanction.
4
Recognize the evidence for the vision
Contrast this with the mutawatir narrations from the Companions about the vision of Allah with the eyes. Al-Ash'ari emphasizes the multiplicity and reliability of these reports.
Mutawatir means mass-transmitted, yielding certainty.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how al-Ash'ari frames the debate as a matter of following transmitted authority versus personal opinion and blind imitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الأول في إبانة قول أهل الزيغ والبدعة
٦- أما بعد : فإن كثيراً من الزائغين عن الحق من المعتزلة وأهل القدر مالت بهم أهواؤهم إلى تقليد رؤسائهم ومن مضى من أسلافهم، فتأولوا القرآن على آرائهم تأويلاً لم يُنزل به الله سلطاناً، ولا أوضح به برهاناً، ولا نقلوه عن رسول رب العالمين، ولا عن السلف المتقدمين فخالفوا روايات الصحابة عن نبي الله صلوات الله عليه وسلامه في رؤية الله عز وجل بالأبصار، وقد جاءت في ذلك الروايات من الجهات المختلفات، وتواترت بها الآثار، وتتابعت بها الأخبار .
The first chapter: explaining the statement of the people of deviation and innovation. 6- To proceed: Indeed, many of those who deviate from the truth among the Mu'tazila and the Qadariyya, their desires led them to follow their leaders and those who passed from their predecessors. So they interpreted the Qur'an according to their own opinions, an interpretation for which Allah sent down no authority, nor made clear any proof, nor did they transmit it from the Messenger of the Lord of the Worlds, nor from the early predecessors. So they contradicted the narrations of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, from the Prophet of Allah, may the blessings and peace of Allah be upon him, concerning the vision of Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, with the eyes, while narrations on that have come from various directions, and the reports have been transmitted successively (mutawatir), and the traditions have followed one another.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is an introductory accusation. Al-Ash'ari begins the chapter by stating its purpose: to expose the false beliefs of the deviant sects, specifically the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya. He explains that their deviation stems from blindly following their leaders and predecessors, leading them to interpret the Qur'an without divine authority or proof. As a result, they contradicted the authentic narrations transmitted from the Companions regarding the vision of Allah on the Day of Judgment. Al-Ash'ari emphasizes that these narrations are numerous, transmitted from different chains, and have reached the status of tawatur (mass transmission), making their denial a rejection of established religious knowledge.

Key Terms
الرؤية
المعتزلة
القدرية
التقليد
التواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila denied the vision of Allah based on rational arguments derived from the Qur'an.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari argues that their denial stems from blind imitation of their leaders and interpreting the Qur'an without authority, contradicting the mutawatir narrations.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari, what is the primary cause of the Mu'tazila's denial of the vision of Allah?
A) Their rational arguments
B) Taqlid of their leaders and lack of transmitted authority
C) Their careful study of the Qur'an
D) Their acceptance of all hadith

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari accuses the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya of denying the vision of Allah due to blind imitation and rejection of mutawatir reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about Allah simply because a respected teacher or scholar taught it, without verifying it from the Qur'an and Sunnah? How does Al-Ash'ari's accusation of taqlid challenge you to examine the sources of your own convictions?
?
Are there any verses of the Qur'an that you find difficult to accept literally—like the vision of Allah—and that you might be interpreting to fit your own reasoning rather than submitting to the transmitted understanding of the Companions? What would it cost you to surrender your intellect to the prophetic tradition?
?
The mutawatir reports on the vision are described as overwhelming. If you have ever doubted this matter due to intellectual arguments, are you prepared to trust the consensus of the early generations over your own logic? What is holding you back from that submission?

The Qadariyyah and the Created Quran
Accusation that Qadariyyah said the Quran is created, like polytheists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari equates the Qadariyyah's claim that the Quran is created with the polytheists' rejection of its divine origin.

Core Idea
Calling the Quran 'created' aligns with polytheists who called it 'human speech'.

In this passage from Al-Ibanah, Imam al-Ash'ari lays out a sharp accusation: the Qadariyyah (including the Mu'tazilah) who say the Quran is created are following the very same reasoning as the polytheists of Mecca. The polytheists dismissed the Quran as mere human speech; the Qadariyyah, by claiming it was created, similarly reduce it to a contingent, human-like product. This lesson examines that comparison and its theological stakes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic phrase and its literal translation. Notice the key terms: 'خلق القرآن' (creation of the Quran) and 'قول البشر' (saying of humans).
The passage is short but packs a strong rhetorical comparison.
2
Identify the comparison
Al-Ash'ari explicitly compares the Qadariyyah to 'their brethren among the polytheists.' Why would he call them brethren?
Think about the shared belief: both groups deny that the Quran is uncreated divine speech.
3
Reflect on the theological point
Consider why this matters in Aqeedah. For Ash'ari, the Quran being uncreated is a core doctrine; equating it with created speech undermines Allah's attribute of speech.
This passage is part of a larger polemic against rationalist theologies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودانوا بخلق القرآن نظيراً لقول إخوانهم من المشركين الذين قالوا: إن هذا إلا قول البشر. فزعموا أن القرآن كقول البشر.
And they adhered to the creation of the Qur'an, analogous to the saying of their brethren among the polytheists who said: 'This is not but the saying of a human.' So they claimed that the Qur'an is like the saying of humans.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an accusation against the Qadariyyah (and Mu'tazilah) that they likened the Qur'an to human speech, aligning with the polytheists' denial of its divine origin. The author points out the similarity between their statement and that of the disbelievers who called the Qur'an 'the saying of a human.'

Key Terms
خلق القرآن
قول البشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Qadariyyah completely denied the Quran is from God, but in fact they affirmed it as God's creation, not as an uncreated attribute.
Correction: The passage shows that their claim of 'creation' is equated with the polytheists' dismissal of it as mere human speech. The issue is not whether it is from God, but whether it is uncreated divine speech.

Checkpoint
To whom did the author compare the Qadariyyah in their claim about the Qur'an?
A) The Majus
B) The polytheists
C) The Jews
D) The Christians

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari condemns the doctrine of the created Quran by equating it with the polytheists' rejection of the Quran as divine speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Ash'ari warns that holding the Quran to be created aligns you with polytheists. Have you ever treated the Quran as a mere book, subject to your interpretation or criticism, rather than as the eternal, uncreated word of Allah? What would change if you truly revered it as such?
?
The polytheists said 'this is not but human speech'. The Qadariyyah said it is 'created' but like human speech. Is there any belief you hold that, even if it sounds Islamic, actually reduces Allah's attributes to something less than they are? Will you examine your heart for such hidden shirk?
?
If the Quran is not like any human word, your response to it cannot be like your response to human words. When you hear the Quran recited, do you listen as if Allah Himself is speaking directly to you, or do you listen as you would to a lecture? Commit to one change in how you listen to the Quran this week.

The Accusation of Dualism: Two Creators for Good and Evil
Imam al-Ash'ari accuses the Qadariyyah of dualistic belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the accusation that the Qadariyyah believe in two separate creators for good and evil, and how this parallels Zoroastrian dualism.

Core Idea
Attributing evil to a separate creator leads to dualism.

Imam al-Ash'ari levels a serious charge against the Qadariyyah: that they effectively believe in two gods—one for good and one for evil—just like the Majus (Zoroastrians). This brief passage, though only a sentence, encapsulates a core theological conflict: is evil willed by Allah, or does it have an independent source? Understanding this accusation helps us see why orthodox Sunni theology insists that everything, including evil, falls under Allah's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and its English translation. Notice the two claims made in one sentence.
2
Identify the two claims
The passage contains two distinct claims: (1) that good and evil have two creators, and (2) that some evils occur that God did not will. Underline these in the translation.
These claims are presented as accusations, not as statements of fact.
3
Consider the comparison to Majus
The author compares the Qadariyyah to the Majus (Zoroastrians), who believed in a god of light (good) and a god of darkness (evil). Ask yourself why this comparison is damaging in an Islamic context.
Zoroastrian dualism was seen as a major heresy by early Muslims.
4
Reflect on the significance for Tawheed
Think about why attributing some events to a separate creator violates the Islamic concept of Tawheed (oneness of God). The commentary will explain this further.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Their Claim of Independent Power Over Actions
Accusation of Qadariyyah claiming independent power, compared to Majus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Ash'ari accuses the Qadariyyah of being like the Majus due to their belief in independent power over actions.

Core Idea
Claiming independent power over actions is a form of hidden dualism.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari confronts a dangerous claim made by the Qadariyyah sect. They asserted that humans alone control their own actions, independent of Allah's will. By doing so, they effectively denied Allah's complete power and resembled the Majus (Zoroastrians) who gave Satan independent power over evil. The Imam forcefully labels them as 'the Majus of this nation.'

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong language used in the accusation.
2
Identify the core accusation
What exactly is the Qadariyyah claim according to the Imam? They 'claimed that they alone have power over their actions without their Lord.'
3
Understand the comparison to Majus
Why does the Imam compare them to Majus? The Majus gave Satan power over evil independent of God; the Qadariyyah gave humans power over actions independent of God. Both affirm a rival power to God.
This comparison is meant to shock and highlight the severity of the deviation.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
What does this accusation reveal about Tawhid? True tawhid requires affirming that Allah alone has absolute power over all actions, human or otherwise.

Commentary
This passage accuses the Qadariyyah of claiming exclusive power over their actions, thereby asserting independence from God. The author compares them to the Majus who gave Satan power over evil that they denied to God, and concludes that they are rightly called the Majus of this nation.

Refuting Dual Creators and Self-Sufficient Power
Al-Ash'ari lists two heretical claims and refutes them with Quran and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two heretical claims that Al-Ash'ari refutes: that good and evil have two creators, and that humans independently possess power to cause benefit or harm, both of which contradict Islamic tawhid.

Core Idea
Denying Allah's sole creation and power is a return to dualism and a rejection of the Quran.

This passage presents two related heresies that Al-Ash'ari attacks. The first claims that good and evil come from separate creators, echoing Magian dualism. The second claims that humans independently control their own benefit and harm, contradicting the Quranic verse that only Allah holds such power. Both claims undermine tawhid and the consensus of Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the overall argument. Note the two distinct claims being refuted.
The passage is accusatory; Al-Ash'ari is identifying the heresy.
2
Identify the first claim: dual creators
Find the phrase about 'good and evil have two creators' and note how Al-Ash'ari connects it to the Magians (Zoroastrians). This is a charge of dualism.
The term 'مجوس' refers to Zoroastrians who believed in two primordial principles.
3
Identify the second claim: self-sufficient power
Find the claim that humans 'possess harm and benefit for themselves without Allah'. Notice the Quranic verse cited in refutation.
The verse from Surah al-A'raf emphasizes that even the Prophet has no independent power.
4
Reflect on the refutation
Al-Ash'ari condemns these claims as rejection of the Quran and consensus. Consider why such beliefs are incompatible with Islamic monotheism.
Consensus (ijma') is a key source of authority in Sunni Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعموا أن للخير والشر خالقين، كما زعمت المجوس ذلك، وأنه يكون من الشرور ما لا يشاء الله، كما قالت المجوس. وزعموا أنهم يملكون الضر والنفع لأنفسهم دون الله عز وجل، رداً لقول الله عز وجل لنبيه: {قُل لَا أَمْلِكُ لِنَفْسِي نَفْعًا وَلَا ضَرًّا إِلَّا مَا شَاءَ اللهُ} [الأعراف: 188] وإعراضاً عن القرآن، وعما أجمع عليه أهل الإسلام.

And they claimed that they possess harm and benefit for themselves without Allah, Mighty and Majestic, in rejection of the saying of Allah, Mighty and Majestic, to His Prophet: {Say: 'I do not possess for myself benefit or harm except what Allah wills'} [al-A'raf: 188] and turning away from the Qur'an and from what the people of Islam have unanimously agreed upon.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is an accusation against a heretical group (likely the Qadariyya or Mu'tazila). Al-Ash'ari lists two of their claims. First, they claimed that good and evil have two separate creators, resembling the dualism of the Magians (Zoroastrians), and that some evils occur without Allah's will. Second, they claimed that human beings possess the power to cause benefit and harm to themselves independently of Allah, contradicting the Qur'anic verse where Allah commands the Prophet to declare that he possesses no such power except by Allah's will. Al-Ash'ari concludes that this is a rejection of the Qur'an and the consensus of Muslims.

Correction: Allah alone is the creator of all things, good and evil, and no one possesses power except by His will, as stated in the Quran and agreed upon by Muslims.

B) That some evils occur without Allah's will

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari refutes the heresy of dual creators and human self-sufficient power by affirming that Allah alone is the creator and controller of all benefit and harm, as taught in the Quran and Muslim consensus.

?

Thirteenth Accusation: Claim of Independence in Actions
Al-Ash'ari accuses the sect of claiming independent power over their actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Ash'ari accuses the sect of claiming independence from Allah and how he compares them to the Magians.

Core Idea
Claiming independence in actions makes one a 'Magian of this Ummah'.

Al-Ash'ari continues his refutation of the Qadari sect by exposing their belief in self-sufficiency. In this passage, he draws a striking parallel to Zoroastrian dualism, labeling the sect as the 'Magians of this Ummah.' This lesson examines the accusation and its implications.

2

The Magians attributed power over evil to the devil; the sect attributes power over their own actions to themselves, denying Allah's omnipotence.
3

Consider why al-Ash'ari considers this claim so severe that he calls them 'Magians of this Ummah.' Think about the implications for tawhid.

Al-Ash'ari's Comprehensive Refutation of the Sects
Al-Ash'ari lists the innovating sects and states his refutation plan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which sects al-Ash'ari considers innovators and how he plans to refute them systematically.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari names the heretical sects and commits to refuting them chapter by chapter.

In this concluding part of his introduction, al-Ash'ari explicitly names the groups he will refute: the Jahmiyyah, Murji'ah, Haruriyyah, Mu'tazilah, and Qadariyyah. He emphasizes that their error lies in contradicting the Qur'an, Sunnah, the practice of the Prophet and Companions, and the consensus of the Ummah. He then declares his systematic approach to refuting each sect one by one, relying on Allah's assistance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Note the sects listed and the three sources they contradicted.
2
Identify the sects and their error
List the five sects mentioned. Understand that their innovation is defined by contradicting the Book, Sunnah, and consensus of the early community.
The passage uses 'ahlu l-bida'' (people of innovation) as a category.
3
Notice al-Ash'ari's method
Observe that he says he will refute them 'chapter by chapter and point by point,' indicating a systematic, thorough approach.
He ends with a prayer for divine help, showing his reliance on Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
-٢٢ وكذلك جميع أهل البدع من الجهمية والمرجئة والحرورية ، أهل الزيغ فيما ابتدعوا وخالفوا الكتاب والسنة، ومـا كـان عليه النبي وأصحابه رضي الله عنهم أجمعين، وأجمعت عليـه الأمـة كفعل المعتزلة والقدرية، وأنا ذاكر ذلك باباً ،باباً، وشيئاً شيئاً إن شاء الله ، وبه المعونة والتأييد ، ومنه التوفيق والتسديد
-22 And likewise all the people of innovation among the Jahmiyyah, the Murji'ah, and the Haruriyyah, people of deviation in what they innovated and contradicted the Book and the Sunnah, and what the Prophet and his Companions, may Allah be pleased with them all, were upon, and what the Ummah agreed upon, like the actions of the Mu'tazilah and the Qadariyyah. And I will mention that chapter by chapter and thing by thing, if Allah wills. And with Him is assistance and support, and from Him is success and guidance.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a concluding statement of the introduction, outlining the author's methodology. Al-Ash'ari groups all heretical sects under 'people of innovation' and names three: Jahmiyyah, Murji'ah, and Haruriyyah (Kharijites). He then adds that they also include the Mu'tazilah and Qadariyyah as examples. He emphasizes that these sects deviated (أهل الزيغ) by innovating and contradicting three sources: the Book (Quran), the Sunnah, and the practice of the Prophet and his Companions, as well as the consensus of the Ummah. He then declares his plan to refute them systematically, chapter by chapter and point by point (باباً باباً وشيئاً شيئاً), ending with a prayer for divine assistance and success.

Key Terms
الجهمية
المرجئة
الحرورية
المعتزلة
القدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Ash'ari views these sects as outside the fold of Islam
Correction: Rather, he engages with them as Muslims who fell into error, aiming to refute their innovations while still considering them part of the Ummah.

Checkpoint

C) The Quran, the Hadith, and the opinions of scholars
D) The Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the Caliphs

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari sets out a systematic refutation of five innovating sects based on their deviation from Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

What steps are you taking to ensure your beliefs are rooted in the Book, Sunnah, and consensus of the Ummah as al-Ash'ari emphasised?
?
Al-Ash'ari planned to refute these sects chapter by chapter, relying on Allah's support. Are you as systematic in protecting your own faith from doubts? Where do you need to turn to Allah for guidance and success today?
?
The people of innovation contradicted the Book, Sunnah, and the way of the Prophet and his Companions. Examine your own life: is there any area where your practice or belief diverges from these three authorities? What will you do about it starting now?

Al-Ash'ari's Method and the Sects of Innovation
Al-Ash'ari lists the innovating sects and outlines his methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari frames his refutation by identifying the major innovating sects and declaring his systematic approach.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari refutes deviation by naming it and then dismantling it chapter by chapter.

In this opening passage of his Ibanah, Imam al-Ash'ari sets the stage for his entire work. He lists the sects he considers innovators—Jahmiyyah, Murji'ah, Haruriyyah, Mu'tazila, Qadariyya—and explains that they have deviated from the Quran, Sunnah, and communal consensus. He then announces his plan to address each group systematically. This lesson unpacks that foundational statement and shows why identifying the opponent is the first step in theological argumentation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sects listed
Read the passage and note the names of the groups al-Ash'ari calls 'people of innovation.' Why does he mention them together? The commentary will explain their distinct errors.
These sects represent major theological deviations in early Islam.
2
Understand the standard of orthodoxy
Al-Ash'ari says these groups contradict 'the Book, the Sunnah, the Prophet and Companions, and the consensus of the community.' What does this fourfold standard reveal about his methodology?
He uses a traditional Sunni benchmark.
3
Note the systematic plan
He will refute them 'chapter by chapter and thing by thing.' What does this promise about the structure of the book?
It indicates a thorough, organized refutation.
4
Reflect on the opening invocation
The passage ends with a prayer for divine help. Why might a theologian begin with such a statement?
It shows reliance on Allah for guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك جميع أهل البدع من الجهمية والمرجئة والحرورية، أهل الزيغ فيما ابتدعوا وخالفوا الكتاب والسنة، وما كان عليه النبي وأصحابه رضي الله عنهم أجمعين، وأجمعت عليه الأمة كفعل المعتزلة والقدرية، وأنا ذاكر ذلك باباً باباً، وشيئاً شيئاً إن شاء الله، وبه المعونة والتأييد، ومنه التوفيق والتسديد
And likewise, all the people of innovation from the Jahmiyyah, the Murji'ah, and the Haruriyyah — people of deviation in what they innovated, contradicting the Book and the Sunnah, and what the Prophet and his Companions, may Allah be pleased with them all, were upon, and what the community unanimously agreed upon, like the acts of the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya. And I will mention that chapter by chapter and thing by thing, if Allah wills. And with Him is the help and support, and from Him is the success and guidance.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a methodological introduction. Al-Ash'ari first identifies the sectarian groups he considers innovators: the Jahmiyyah (followers of Jahm ibn Safwan, who held extreme determinism), the Murji'ah (who deferred judgment on grave sinners), and the Haruriyyah (the Khawarij, who rebelled against Ali). He describes them as 'people of deviation' because they introduced beliefs that contradict the Quran, the Sunnah, the practice of the Prophet and his Companions, and the consensus of the Muslim community (umma). He also mentions the Mu'tazila and Qadariyya as analogous cases. The author then declares his plan to address these groups systematically, 'chapter by chapter and thing by thing,' signifying a structured refutation. He concludes by invoking divine assistance and guidance.

Key Terms
أهل البدع
الجهمية
المرجئة
الحرورية
المعتزلة
القدرية
الزيغ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage is merely a list of sect names without deeper meaning.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari is deliberately framing his refutation project by naming the specific deviant groups he will address, establishing his methodology based on Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.

Checkpoint

A) Jahmiyyah
B) Murji'ah
C) Rafida
D) Haruriyyah

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari opens his refutation by naming the innovating sects and committing to a systematic, chapter-by-chapter critique grounded in the Quran, Sunnah, and community consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone whose beliefs differ from the Quran and Sunnah, do you approach them with the same humility and reliance on Allah that al-Ash'ari demonstrates by saying 'with Him is the help'? Or do you trust your own arguments?
?
This passage names specific sects. Are there any beliefs or practices in your own life that might unknowingly align with these sects' innovations? Can you honestly examine yourself today and identify any?
?
Al-Ash'ari commits to refuting deviation 'chapter by chapter'. What is one area of your faith where you need to systematically discard an incorrect idea and commit to the truth, even if it requires hard work over time?

The Four Rightly Guided Caliphs and Their Prophetic Caliphate
Affirms the succession and prophetic nature of the four caliphs' rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the order of the four Rightly Guided Caliphs and the concept of prophetic caliphate as affirmed by Imam al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
The caliphate of Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali is the prophetic caliphate.

Imam al-Ash'ari begins by affirming the succession of the four caliphs after the Prophet. He highlights how Abu Bakr was advanced by the Prophet himself and by the Muslims, and he states that the caliphate of these four is a continuation of prophetic authority. This passage also clarifies that Uthman was killed wrongfully, a position important for Sunni identity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the translation. Let the author's own words establish the order and virtues.
Notice the concise yet comprehensive style.
2
Identify the four caliphs
List the four caliphs in the order given. Note the specific virtue or description mentioned for each: Abu Bakr (advanced for prayer, against apostates), Umar (mentioned), Uthman (killed wrongfully), Ali (mentioned).
3
Understand 'khilafat nubuwwa'
Focus on the concluding phrase: 'their caliphate is the caliphate of prophethood.' Reflect on what this implies about their authority and legitimacy.
This concept distinguishes the first four caliphs from later rulers.
4
Reflect on the statement about Uthman
Why does al-Ash'ari explicitly say that those who killed Uthman did so wrongfully? Consider the sectarian context and the importance of this point for Sunni theology.
This guards against the belief that Uthman deserved his fate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقول: إن الإمام الفاضل بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أبو بكر الصديق رضوان الله عليه وإن الله سبحانه وتعالى أعز به الدين، وأظهره على المرتدين، وقدمه المسلمون للإمامة، كما قدمه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم للصلاة، وسموه بأجمعهم خليفة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه ثم عثمان عفان نصر الله وجهه وأن الذين قتلوه قتلوه ظلماً ثم علي بن أبي طالب رضي الله عنه فهؤلاء الأئمة بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وخلافتهم خلافة النبوة
And we say: Indeed the excellent Imam after the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, and indeed Allah, Glorified and Exalted, strengthened the religion through him, and manifested him against the apostates, and the Muslims advanced him to imamate just as the Messenger of Allah advanced him for prayer, and they all called him the Successor of the Messenger of Allah. Then Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, then Uthman ibn Affan, may Allah honor his face, and indeed those who killed him killed him wrongfully, then Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him. These are the Imams after the Messenger of Allah, and their caliphate is the caliphate of prophethood.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage declares the order and virtues of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. It emphasizes that Abu Bakr was advanced by the Prophet for prayer and by the Muslims for imamate, and that the caliphate of these four is a prophetic caliphate (khilafat nubuwwa). It also states that Uthman was killed wrongfully.

الخلافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage implies that caliphs after Ali are not legitimate.
Correction: The passage only affirms that the first four caliphs have a special status as prophetic caliphate, but does not deny the legitimacy of later caliphs.

Checkpoint

B) He was killed justly.

D) He abdicated.

Key Takeaway
The four Rightly Guided Caliphs—Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali—held a prophetic caliphate, and Uthman was killed unjustly.

?

?

?
The prophetic caliphate is a trust. In what area of your life are you most neglecting to uphold that trust, and what specific change will you make this week to align your actions with the guidance these four Imams embodied?

The Order and Legitimacy of the Four Rightly Guided Caliphs
Imam al-Ash'ari enumerates the four caliphs in order and affirms their prophetic caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position on the order and legitimacy of the first four caliphs and the basis for their imamate.

Core Idea
The caliphate of the four rightly guided caliphs is a prophetic caliphate, and their order is fixed.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari's al-Ibanah outlines the Sunni consensus on the imamate of Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali (may Allah be pleased with them). It affirms their legitimate succession to the Prophet and refutes any claims that disrupt this order. By examining the text, we see how the early community recognized Abu Bakr's precedence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Imam Ash'ari uses a declarative style affirming the order.
2
Identify the four caliphs and their order
The passage lists the four caliphs in a specific sequence. Find each name and note the order: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali.
The passage explicitly states that these are the imams after the Prophet.
3
Examine the proofs for Abu Bakr's imamate
The passage gives several proofs: Allah strengthened the religion through him, he prevailed over apostates, the Muslims advanced him for imamate as the Prophet advanced him for prayer, and they called him Caliph of the Messenger.
This establishes the basis for his precedence.
4
Note the statement about Uthman's killing
The passage explicitly states that those who killed Uthman did so wrongfully and aggressively. This affirms his innocence and the injustice of his death.
This refutes any justification for rebellion.
5
Understand the final affirmation
The passage concludes by stating that these four are the imams and their caliphate is a prophetic caliphate, meaning it follows the prophetic model.
This emphasizes the legitimacy and continuity of their rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقول : إن الإمام الفاضل بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أبو بكر الصديق رضوان الله عليه وإن الله سبحانه وتعالى أعز به الدين، وأظهره على المرتدين، وقدمه المسلمون للإمامة، كما قدمه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم للصلاة، وسموه بأجمعهم خليفة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. ثم عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه. ثم عثمان بن عفان نصر الله وجهه، وأن الذين قتلوه قتلوه ظلماً وعدوانا. ثم علي بن أبي طالب رضي الله عنه. فهؤلاء الأئمة بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وخلافتهم خلافة النبوة.
And we say: Indeed, the eminent Imam after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him). And indeed Allah (glorified and exalted) strengthened the religion through him, and made him prevail over the apostates. Then 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him). These are the imams after the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and their caliphate is a prophetic caliphate.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement affirming the order and legitimacy of the first four caliphs. The author begins by stating that Abu Bakr is the foremost imam after the Prophet, supported by divine aid and chosen by Muslims for leadership, paralleling the Prophet's own choice of him to lead prayer. He then lists 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali in sequence, explicitly stating that 'Uthman was killed unjustly. The passage concludes by affirming that these four are the rightful imams and that their caliphate is a continuation of the prophetic mission.

خلافة النبوة (prophetic caliphate)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may deny the legitimacy of one of the four caliphs or alter their order.
Correction: The passage affirms the consensus on the order and legitimacy, supported by the practice of the early Muslims and the Prophet's own indication.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The order of the four caliphs is fixed, and their caliphate is a prophetic caliphate, affirming the Sunni doctrine of legitimate succession after the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Love for the Companions and the Rightly Guided Caliphs
Imam Ash'ari states love for all Companions, witnesses paradise for the ten, and affirms the virtue of the four caliphs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the Companions: loving all, witnessing Paradise for the ten, refraining from their disputes, and affirming the unique virtue of the four caliphs.

Core Idea
Sunni love for all Companions, silence on their disputes, and special honor for the ten and the four caliphs.

Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, in his work Al-Ibanah, lays down the foundational Sunni attitude towards the Companions. This passage summarizes key points: general love, specific testimony of Paradise for the ten, avoiding judgment of past conflicts, and the unparalleled virtue of the four rightly-guided caliphs. Let's examine each element.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text aloud if possible, then follow the literal translation. Notice the rhythm of affirmations.
2
Identify the four affirmations
The passage makes four distinct statements: praising all Companions, witnessing Paradise for the ten, befriending all others, and refraining from disputes. Then it declares the four caliphs as unmatched in virtue.
3
Understand 'refraining from disputes'
The phrase 'ونكف عما شجر بينهم' is a key Sunni principle: we do not take sides or speak ill of Companions regarding their historical conflicts.
This guards against sectarian divisions.
4
Grasp the unique status of the four caliphs
The passage asserts that the four caliphs (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali) are rightly-guided and guided, and none equals them in virtue. This affirms their precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونثني عليهم بما أثنى الله به عليهم ونتولاهم أجمعين. ونشهد بالجنة للعشرة الذين شهد لهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بها، ونتولى سائر أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، ونكف عما شجر بينهم. وندين بأن الأئمة الأربعة خلفاء راشدون مهديون فضلاء، لا يوازيهم في الفضل غيرهم.
And we praise them with what Allah has praised them with, and we befriend them all. And we bear witness of Paradise for the ten whom the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) bore witness to. And we befriend the rest of the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and we refrain from [discussing] what occurred among them. And we hold as religion that the four Imams are rightly-guided caliphs, guided ones, virtuous ones; none equals them in virtue.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage establishes the Sunni position on the Companions. First, the author declares general praise and loyalty to all Companions. Then he specifically affirms that the ten Companions promised Paradise by the Prophet are indeed in Paradise. He extends loyalty to all other Companions and refrains from judging their historical disputes. Finally, he emphasizes the unique virtue of the four caliphs, calling them rightly-guided and guided, and asserts that no one can match their merit.

Key Terms
صحابة (Companions)
شهادة بالجنة (testimony of Paradise)
خلفاء راشدون (rightly-guided caliphs)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Sunnis curse or condemn some Companions, or that all Companions are equal in virtue.
Correction: This passage shows that Sunnis love all Companions, refrain from judging their disputes, and affirm the special virtue of the four caliphs and the ten promised Paradise.

Checkpoint

D) He considers only the ten Companions as reliable

Key Takeaway
The Sunni path is love for all Companions, silence on their disputes, and acknowledgment of the special virtue of the ten and the four caliphs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Befriending the Companions and Refraining from Disputes
Imam Ash'ari states the Sunni stance on companions and the four caliphs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sunnis befriend all Companions and refrain from discussing their conflicts.

Core Idea
Love all Companions; leave their disputes to Allah.

In this passage, Imam Ash'ari articulates a core Sunni principle: we hold affection for every Companion of the Prophet and we do not delve into the disagreements that occurred among them. This teaching protects the honor of the Sahaba and promotes unity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the full passage once to get the gist. Notice the two verbs: نَتَوَلَّى (we befriend) and نَكُفُّ (we refrain).
2
Understand 'befriending' (tawalla)
Befriending means loving, supporting, and defending all Companions. It includes acknowledging their virtues and praying for them.
3
Understand 'refraining' (kafaf)
Refraining means not discussing the disputes that occurred among them. This is an act of respect and trust in Allah's judgment.
This does not mean we are unaware; it means we do not engage in blame or partisanship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بينهم ونتولى سائر أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، ونكف عما شجر وندين بأن الأئمة الأربعة خلفاء راشدون مهديون فضلاء، لا يوازيهم في الفضل غيرهم.
Among them: we befriend all the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and refrain from what occurred between them, and we hold that the four Imams are rightly-guided, divinely-directed, virtuous caliphs, none equal to them in virtue.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a concise creedal statement about the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the four rightly-guided caliphs. Imam Ash'ari begins by declaring the Sunni position of befriending (tawalla) all the Companions and refraining (kafaf) from discussing the disputes that occurred among them. This reflects the principle of 'imsaak' (silence) regarding the conflicts among the Companions, as their status and efforts are left to Allah. Then he specifically affirms that the four caliphs—Abu Bakr, 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with them)—are rightly-guided (rashidun), guided to the truth (mahdiyyun), and virtuous (fudala'), and that no one else equals them in virtue. This establishes their superiority over all other members of the Muslim community after the Prophet.

Key Terms
تولى
كف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think we must take sides in the disputes among the Companions or criticize some of them.
Correction: Imam Ash'ari teaches that we refrain from discussing these disputes entirely, as they are between the Companions themselves and are not for us to judge.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ash'ari, what is the proper attitude towards the disputes that occurred among the Companions?
A) We analyze them to determine who was right.
B) We refrain from discussing them.
C) We criticize the wrongdoers.
D) We remain neutral but judge privately.

Key Takeaway
Sunnis befriend all Companions and avoid discussing their disagreements, trusting Allah to judge between them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear or read about disagreements among the Companions, does your heart incline to take sides or criticize any of them? What can you do from now on to replace that impulse with love and restraint?
?
This lesson teaches you to befriend all Companions. Is there a Companion (like Muawiyah or Aisha) about whom you have negative feelings? Will you commit to purifying your heart and leaving their matters to Allah?
?
Think of a recent conversation where Muslims debated historical figures. How can you apply the principle of 'refraining from disputes' in such discussions, even when others may not agree? What will you say or do differently?

The Virtue and Status of the Four Rightly Guided Caliphs
Imam Ash'ari states the Sunni stance on companions and the four caliphs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni belief in the unique superiority of the four caliphs over all other Companions.

Core Idea
The four caliphs are the best of the Companions, none equal to them.

Imam Ash'ari specifies that the four caliphs—Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali—are not only leaders but are rightly-guided, divinely-directed, and virtuous. He then asserts that no one else from the Ummah matches their virtue. This establishes their special rank among the Sahaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four caliphs
The phrase 'al-a'immah al-arba'ah' refers to Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali (may Allah be pleased with them).

2
Understand the three attributes
They are described as rashidun (rightly-guided), mahdiyyun (divinely-directed), and fudala' (virtuous).
3
Grasp the claim of superiority
The phrase 'la yuwaazihim fi al-fadl ghayruhum' means no one else equals them in virtue. This is a clear statement of their precedence.
This does not deny the virtue of other Companions, but affirms that the caliphs are the best.

Praying Behind Any Imam
Imam Ash'ari affirms praying behind any imam regardless of piety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on praying behind an imam regardless of his personal righteousness, based on the practice of the companions.

Core Idea
The validity of prayer does not depend on the imam's piety.

Imam Ash'ari presents a core Sunni creedal principle: the permissibility and validity of congregational prayer behind any imam, whether righteous or wicked. This teaching distinguishes Sunni Islam from sectarian groups that reject prayer behind sinful leaders. The practice of the companion 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar serves as a definitive precedent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the inclusive phrase 'كل بر وفاجر' (every righteous and wicked person).
This phrase is the doctrinal core.
2
Identify the authorities
The passage combines a creedal statement from Imam Ash'ari with a narration from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, a senior companion.
Ibn 'Umar's practice is used as a proof.
3
Understand the historical context
Al-Hajjaj ibn Yusuf was a notoriously oppressive governor. Ibn 'Umar praying behind him shows that the principle applies even in extreme cases.
This is a strong counter to the Kharijite position.
4
Reflect on the sectarian implications
This teaching rejects the Kharijite and Mu'tazilite views that prayer behind a sinful imam is invalid.
It preserves community unity.
5
Apply the lesson to daily life
Consider how this principle fosters unity in the Muslim community, especially when leaders are imperfect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ديننا أن نصلي الجمعة والأعياد خلف كل بر وفاجر، كذلك وسائر الصلوات والجماعات كما روي عن عبد الله بن عمر رضي الله عنهما أنه كان يصلي خلف الحجاج.
And it is part of our religion to pray Friday and the two 'Eids behind every righteous and wicked person, and likewise all other prayers and congregations, as narrated from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) that he used to pray behind al-Hajjaj.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a creedal statement about the validity of praying behind an imam who may be sinful. Imam Ash'ari declares that it is part of the Sunni religion (min dinina) to perform the Friday prayer and the two 'Eid prayers behind any imam, whether he is righteous (birr) or wicked (fajir). He extends this to all prayers and congregational acts. He supports this with the practice of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (a senior companion) who prayed behind al-Hajjaj ibn Yusuf al-Thaqafi, a notoriously oppressive governor. This establishes that the validity of the prayer does not depend on the personal righteousness of the imam, a principle that counters the Kharijite and some Mu'tazilite positions that reject prayer behind a sinful leader.

Key Terms
بر
فاجر
جمعة
عيد
صلاة خلف الفاجر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think it is prohibited to pray behind a sinful imam; the prayer is invalid.
Correction: The Sunni position is that it is permissible and the prayer is valid, as demonstrated by Ibn 'Umar's practice.

Checkpoint
Whose practice did Imam Ash'ari cite to support praying behind a wicked imam?
A) Abu Bakr al-Siddiq
B) 'Umar ibn al-Khattab
C) 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar
D) 'Ali ibn Abi Talib

Key Takeaway
In Sunni Islam, the validity of congregational prayer is not contingent on the imam's personal righteousness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever avoided a congregational prayer because you judged the imam's character? How does the action of Abdullah ibn Umar challenge that attitude? Will you now commit to praying behind any Muslim imam, leaving judgment to Allah?
?
If your heart feels resistance to this teaching, what does it reveal about your pride? Are you willing to humble yourself and prioritize community unity over personal judgment?
?
The lesson shows that the validity of worship is not tied to the leader's righteousness. How does this truth free you from the burden of policing others' sins? What step will you take this week to act on this freedom?

Supplication for Rulers and Prohibition of Rebellion
Imam Ash'ari commands supplication for rulers, acknowledges their imamate, and prohibits rebellion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical Sunni position on political authority: that loyalty is maintained through supplication and acknowledgment of rulers, and that armed rebellion is categorically rejected, even against unjust rulers.

Core Idea
Armed rebellion is misguidance; loyalty is prayer, not the sword.

Imam al-Ash'ari presents the Sunni stance on leadership during his era, a time of political turbulence. This passage establishes that while rulers may fall short of justice, the proper response is supplication for their righteousness and rejection of rebellion. The text directly counters those who advocate armed revolt, declaring such views misguided.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the passage once without analysis. Let the author's words set the frame.
2
Identify the distinct positions
The passage contains multiple elements: supplication, acknowledgment, declaration of misguidance, and rejection of armed rebellion. List them.
3
Understand the condition of 'lack of uprightness'
Note that even when rulers show deviation, rebellion is still rejected. This is a key point.
The passage says 'if they show lack of uprightness' but does not make rebellion permissible.
4
Reflect on the concept of fitna
Consider why abandoning fighting in fitna is emphasized. How does this protect the community?
Fitna here means civil strife and chaos.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونرى الدعاء لأئمة المسلمين بالصلاح والإقرار بإمامتهم، وتضليل من رأى الخروج عليهم، إذا ظهر منهم ترك الاستقامة. وندين بإنكار الخروج بالسيف، وترك القتال في الفتنة.
And we hold the supplication for the leaders of the Muslims for their righteousness and acknowledgement of their imamate, and we declare misguided those who see rebellion against them when a lack of uprightness appears from them. And we adhere to the rejection of rebellion with the sword and abandoning fighting in times of tribulation (fitna).
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage outlines the Sunni political doctrine regarding rulers and rebellion. Imam Ash'ari states three positions: (1) They pray for the rulers' righteousness (ṣalāḥ) and acknowledge their imamate (iqrār bi-imāmatihim). (2) They declare as misguided (taḍlīl) those who advocate rebellion (kharūj) against rulers when the rulers show lack of uprightness (tark al-istiqāma). This is a clear condemnation of armed revolt, even against unjust rulers. (3) They adhere to (yadīnūn bi-) the rejection of rebellion with the sword (inkār al-khurūj bil-sayf) and abandoning fighting in times of fitna (tribulation). This reflects the classical Sunni principle of patience with oppressive rulers and avoidance of civil strife.

القتال في الفتنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that rebelling against an unjust ruler is an Islamic duty.
Correction: This passage declares such rebellion misguidance, and commands supplication and patience instead.

Checkpoint

B) They are misguided.
C) They should be supported.
D) They are forgiven if they repent.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni creed mandates loyalty to rulers through supplication and forbids armed rebellion, even against unjust rulers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Abandoning fighting in fitna requires immense patience. Think of a time of communal conflict you witnessed or heard about. Were you quick to take sides or eager to fight? This lesson demands that you hold back. How can you train yourself to remain neutral and pray instead of engaging in division?

Wiping over Khuffs as an Established Sunnah
Al-Ash'ari affirms wiping over khuffs as sunnah in all circumstances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Ash'ari's affirmation that wiping over leather socks (khuffs) is a confirmed Sunnah in all circumstances, and the sectarian context of this belief.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a confirmed Sunnah both at home and while traveling.

Al-Ash'ari includes in his creed an important practical matter of purification. He firmly states that wiping over the special leather socks (khuffs) during ablution is an established prophetic practice, valid both when one is settled and when traveling. This directly counters those who rejected this practice, particularly the Kharijites.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic sentence and its literal English translation. Notice the concise creedal style.
The passage is a single statement of belief.
2
Understand the key terms
Identify the meaning of 'khuffs' (leather socks), 'sunnah' (prophetic practice), and the conditions 'hader' (residence) and 'safar' (travel).
These terms are central to the ruling.
3
Grasp the sectarian context
Learn that Al-Ash'ari is refuting the Kharijites, who rejected wiping over khuffs entirely. This shows how creedal statements address practical disagreements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن المسح على الخفين سنة في الحضر والسفر، خلافاً لقول من أنكر ذلك
And that wiping over the khuffs (leather socks) is a sunnah in residence and travel, contrary to the statement of those who deny that.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is another article of faith. Al-Ash'ari declares that wiping over the khuffs (special leather socks worn during ablution) is an established sunnah (prophetic practice) both when one is at home (hader) and when traveling (musafir). He explicitly states that this is in opposition to those who deny this practice. The deniers are identified in the footnote as the Kharijites, who rejected wiping over the khuffs entirely. This affirmation underscores the Sunni position that wiping over socks is a legitimate concession and a confirmed sunnah from the Prophet, not abrogated or invalid.

Key Terms

حضر
سفر

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari affirms that wiping over khuffs is a confirmed Sunnah valid both in residence and travel, countering those who reject it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Prayers for Rulers and Forbidding Rebellion
Al-Ash'ari mandates prayers for rulers and forbids armed rebellion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical Sunni doctrine regarding Muslim rulers: praying for them, acknowledging their authority, and forbidding armed rebellion even when they are unjust.

Core Idea
Pray for rulers, never rebel with the sword.

Among the most sensitive topics in Islamic theology is the relationship with rulers. In this short but powerful passage, Imam al-Ash'ari lays down the Sunni position: we must continuously pray for our leaders, recognize their authority, and categorically reject armed rebellion—even when they deviate from the right path. The text also warns against participating in civil strife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its English translation once. Notice the three distinct commands: prayer, acknowledgment, and forbidding rebellion.
The passage is a creedal statement, so each part carries theological weight.
2
Understand the three components
Identify each component: (1) supplication for rulers' uprightness, (2) affirming their leadership, (3) declaring misguided those who advocate rebellion.
Al-Ash'ari uses the strong term 'tadlil' (declaring misguided) for advocates of rebellion.
3
Explore the reasoning behind forbidding rebellion
Consider why rebellion is forbidden even when rulers lack uprightness. The text ties this to avoiding fitna (civil strife) and maintaining communal stability.
This is a key distinguishing feature of Sunni political theology.
4
Reflect on the practical implication
Ask yourself how this teaching applies in contexts of perceived injustice. The lesson is about patience and prayer rather than confrontation.
This passage is often cited in discussions about political quietism in Sunni Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونرى الدعاء لأئمة المسلمين بالصلاح والإقرار بإمامتهم، وتضليل من رأى الخروج عليهم، إذا ظهر منهم ترك الاستقامة. وندين بإنكار الخروج بالسيف، وترك القتال في الفتنة.
And we are of the view of supplicating for the Muslim leaders for uprightness, and acknowledging their leadership, and declaring misguided those who hold the view of rebelling against them when a lack of uprightness appears from them. And we adhere to forbidding rebellion with the sword, and abandoning fighting in civil strife (fitna).
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement on political theology. Al-Ash'ari outlines the Sunni position regarding Muslim rulers. First, it is part of their creed to pray for the rulers (a'immah) to be righteous (salah) and to recognize their authority (iqrar bi-imamatihim). Second, they consider misguided (tadlil) those who advocate rebellion (khuruj) against the rulers, even if the rulers deviate from the straight path (tark al-istiqamah). Third, they adhere to forbidding armed rebellion (inkar al-khuruj bil-saif) and abstaining from fighting during times of civil strife (fitna). This reflects the classical Sunni doctrine of patience and obedience to avoid bloodshed, prioritizing communal stability over confronting unjust rulers.

Key Terms
أئمة المسلمين
دعاء
خروج
فتنة
استقامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think rebellion is justified against unjust rulers.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari explicitly declares such a view misguided and forbids armed rebellion, even when rulers lack uprightness.

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory.
B) It is permissible if he is sinful.
C) It is forbidden and those who advocate it are misguided.
D) It is recommended as a last resort.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari teaches that Muslims must pray for their rulers and never rebel with the sword, even when the rulers are unjust.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a leader acting unjustly, does your heart immediately lean towards criticizing them publicly or even wishing for their downfall? ?
The passage forbids fighting in fitna. Think of a current situation in the Muslim world where there is civil strife. Instead of taking sides or hoping for one group's victory, what does this lesson ask of you personally? Write down one specific du'a you will make tonight for the Muslims in that conflict.
