Ibn Asakir's Praise of al-Ash'ari's Creed and Fairness
Ibn Asakir extols al-Ash'ari's creed and his fairness toward Imam Ahmad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir praised al-Ash'ari's creed as clear and his fairness towards Imam Ahmad, demonstrating their agreement in the principles of the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Ibn Asakir shows al-Ash'ari's creed is clear and he acknowledged Ahmad.

Ibn Asakir, a renowned historian, writes an editorial commentary on al-Ash'ari's creed. He calls on readers to reflect on its clarity and to acknowledge al-Ash'ari's virtue. He also highlights al-Ash'ari's fairness in recognizing Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal's merit, showing their agreement in creed. This passage helps us see the respect between early Ash'ari and Hanbali scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the creed
Read the Arabic passage that praises the creed. Note the exclamations about its clarity.
The verse from Az-Zumar is quoted to encourage following the best.
2
Identify how Ibn Asakir describes the creed
He uses words like 'clear' (waḍiḥ) and 'manifest' (bayyin). He calls al-Ash'ari an Imam and scholar.
3
Notice al-Ash'ari's fairness
Ibn Asakir says that al-Ash'ari described Ahmad with virtue and acknowledged him, showing fairness.
This is evidence of mutual respect.
4
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that they were in agreement on creed and the principles of religion.
This refutes claims of opposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعد ذلك قال الحافظ هبة الله بن عساكر - رحمه الله تعالى -: فتأملوا رحمكم الله هذا الاعتقاد : ما أوضحه وأبينه واعترفوا بفضل هذا الإمام العالم الذي شرحه وبينه وانظروا سهولة لفظه فما أفصحه وأحسنه، وكونوا ممن قال الله فيهم : ( الَّذِينَ يَسْتَمِعُونَ الْقَوْلَ فَيَتَّبِعُونَ أَحْسَنَهُ ﴾ [الزمر : ۱۸] وتبينوا فضل أبي الحسن واعرفوا إنصافه، واسمعوا وصفه لأحمد بالفضل واعترافه، لتعلموا أنهما كانا في الاعتقاد متفقين وفي أصول الدين ومذهب السنة غير مفترقين، ولم تزل الحنابلة ببغداد في قديم الدهر على ممر الأوقات تعتضد بالأشعرية على أصحاب البدع ؛ لأنهم المتكلمون من أهل الإثبات فمن تكلم منهم في الرد على مبتدع فبلسان الأشعرية يتكلم، ومن حقق منهم في الأصول في مسألة فمنهم يتعلم. اهـ. (التبيين) ص(١٦٣).
After that, al-Hafiz Hibatullah ibn 'Asakir - may Allah have mercy on him - said: 'Reflect, may Allah have mercy on you, upon this creed: how clear and manifest it is! And acknowledge the virtue of this Imam, the scholar, who explained and clarified it. And observe the ease of his wording: how eloquent and beautiful it is! And be among those of whom Allah said: {Those who listen to the word and follow the best thereof} [Az-Zumar 39:18]. And discern the virtue of Abul Hasan and recognize his fairness. And hear his description of Ahmad (ibn Hanbal) with virtue and his acknowledgment, so that you may know that they were in agreement in creed and in the principles of religion and the Sunnah, not divergent. And the Hanbalis in Baghdad from ancient times, over the course of ages, have relied on the Ash'aris against the people of innovation, because they are the theologians (mutakallimun) among the people of affirmation. So whoever among them spoke in refutation of an innovator spoke with the tongue of the Ash'aris, and whoever among them investigated the principles in a matter learned from them.' End. (At-Tabyin) p. 163.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is an editorial comment by al-Hafiz Ibn Asakir. He praises the creed (i'tiqad) presented by al-Ash'ari as clear and eloquent. He then highlights al-Ash'ari's fairness in acknowledging Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal's virtue, noting their agreement in creed and principles of the Sunnah. Ibn Asakir further explains the historical relationship: the Hanbalis of Baghdad relied on the Ash'aris against innovators because the Ash'aris were the theologians of affirmation (ahl al-ithbat). This shows cooperation rather than conflict between the two groups. The passage concludes with an important point: Hanbalis who refuted innovators used the tongue of the Ash'aris, and those who investigated principles learned from them, emphasizing the unity of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Key Terms
الاعتقاد
الإنصاف
أصول الدين
مذهب السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Ash'ari and Ahmad ibn Hanbal were opposed in creed.
Correction: Ibn Asakir explicitly states they were in agreement and not divergent.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what does al-Ash'ari's description of Ahmad show?
A) That al-Ash'ari criticized Ahmad
B) That al-Ash'ari acknowledged Ahmad's virtue and fairness
C) That they disagreed on principles
D) That al-Ash'ari ignored Ahmad

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir emphasizes that al-Ash'ari and Imam Ahmad were united in creed and principles, with al-Ash'ari acknowledging Ahmad's virtue.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage emphasizes that al-Ash'ari and Ahmad were united in creed and principles. Do you contribute to disunity among Muslims by exaggerating differences? How can you emulate al-Ash'ari's fairness in your own conversations about theological disagreements, especially when discussing scholars or schools of thought?

Hanbali Reliance on Ash'aris Against Innovators
Ibn Asakir notes Hanbali reliance on Ash'aris against innovators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's account of the historical cooperation between Hanbalis and Ash'aris, where Hanbalis relied on Ash'ari theologians to refute innovators.

Core Idea
Hanbalis relied on Ash'aris as their theologians against innovators.

Ibn Asakir continues his commentary by addressing the historical relationship between the Hanbalis and Ash'aris. He notes that the Hanbalis in Baghdad consistently sought support from the Ash'aris when confronting innovators, because the Ash'aris were the skilled theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah. This passage highlights a cooperative dynamic rather than conflict.

4

This shows the Ash'aris were teachers in theology.

Mu'tazila Refuted by Their Own Evidence
Shows the Mu'tazila are refuted by the hadith they cite because it affirms Allah is light

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari author turns the Mu'tazila's own proof-text against them by highlighting their inconsistency.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila are refuted by the very hadith they cite because they deny its literal meaning.

This passage concludes the discussion on the hadith 'Light, how can I see Him?' by showing that it actually undermines the Mu'tazila position. Since they deny that Allah is light in reality, citing a hadith that describes Allah as light only exposes their inconsistency. Let's see how the author makes this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the core claim.
Notice how the author directly states the narration is against the Mu'tazila.
2
Identify the key claim
The author claims the narration is against the Mu'tazila, not for them. Why? Because they deny Allah is light in reality.
3
Reflect on the logical trap
The Mu'tazila use a hadith that affirms Allah is light, but they reject the literal meaning of 'light'. This inconsistency makes their argument self-defeating.
This is a classic refutation by showing internal contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أن هذه الرواية على المعتزلة لا لهم ؛ لأنهم ينكرون أن الله نور في الحقيقة. فإذا احتجوا بخبر هم له تاركون وعنه منحرفون كانوا محجوجين
Moreover, this narration is against the Mu'tazila, not for them; because they deny that Allah is light in reality. So if they argue using a report which they themselves abandon and deviate from, they are refuted.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This concluding passage turns the Mu'tazila's own argument against them. They cite the hadith 'Light, how can I see Him?' to deny vision, but the hadith explicitly describes Allah as light. The Mu'tazila, however, deny that Allah is light in a literal sense, since they reject anthropomorphic attributes. Therefore, they are inconsistent: they use a hadith while rejecting its very content. Thus, their citation works against them.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
نور
حقيقة
محجوجين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila can use the hadith 'Nur anna arahu' as evidence while rejecting the literal meaning of 'light'.
Correction: The hadith describes Allah as light; by using it while denying that Allah is light in reality, the Mu'tazila are inconsistent and thus refuted.

Checkpoint
Why is the hadith 'Light, how can I see Him' considered evidence against the Mu'tazila?
A) Because they accept the hadith but deny its content that Allah is light.
B) Because they reject the hadith entirely.
C) Because the hadith proves the impossibility of vision.
D) Because the hadith is about the Prophet's vision.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's citation of the hadith backfires because they deny its literal meaning, making them inconsistent and their argument self-defeating.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself citing a verse or hadith while ignoring or reinterpreting its plain meaning to fit your preferences? What does this passage teach you about the danger of such inconsistency? Commit today to accept the clear teachings of the Qur'an and Sunnah fully, even when they challenge you.
?
The Mu'tazila were exposed by their own evidence. Is there an area of your life where your actions contradict what you claim to believe? How can you bring genuine consistency between your profession of faith and your daily conduct? Write one specific change you will make this week.
?
If you were to be judged by the same standard of consistency applied to the Mu'tazila, would you be refuted or vindicated? What would it take for you to submit completely to the literal meanings of revelation without mental reservations? Ask Allah for sincerity and courage to follow the truth wherever it leads.

Second Argument: Absurd Consequences of a Created Qur'an
Second rejoinder using reductio ad absurdum against createdness of Qur'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Jahmiyyah's claim that the Qur'an is created leads to absurd conclusions that are impossible for the eternal speech of Allah.

Core Idea
If the Qur'an were created, it would be a body or attribute—both lead to absurdities.

Imam al-Ash'ari presents a second rejoinder against those who claim the Qur'an is created. He shows that if it were created, it would either be a body or an attribute of a body. Both options force the Jahmiyyah to accept impossible consequences, proving that the Qur'an cannot be created. Let's examine this logical argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the flow of the reductio argument come through.
2
Identify the two options
Note that the author presents two possibilities if the Qur'an is created: it must be either a body or an attribute of a body. This is the starting point of the argument.
These two options cover all possibilities for a created entity.
3
Trace the absurd consequences for each option
For the body option: if it is a body, it could be a speaker, and Allah could transform it into a human, jinn, or devil. For the attribute option: Allah could turn that attribute into a body that eats, drinks, and dies.
These consequences are clearly impossible for the speech of Allah.
4
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
The Jahmiyyah are forced to accept these consequences, but they are impermissible for Allah's speech. Therefore, the initial assumption (that the Qur'an is created) must be false.
This confirms the doctrine that the Qur'an is uncreated and eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب : ويقال لهم أيضاً : لو كان كلام الله مخلوقاً لكان جسماً أو نعتاً لجسم ولو كان جسماً لجاز أن يكون متكلماً، والله قادر على قلبهما، وفي هذا ما يلزمهم، ويجب عليهم أن يجوزوا أن يقلب الله القرآن إنساناً أو جنياً أو شيطاناً، تعالى الله عز وجل أن يكون كلامه كذلك ولو كان نعتاً لجسم كالنعوت؛ فالله قادر على أن يجعلها أجساما (١) ، فكان يجب على الجهمية أن يجوزوا أن يجعل الله القرآن جسماً متجسداً يأكل ويشرب وأن يجعله إنسانا ويميته، وهذا ما لا يجوز على كلام الله تعالى عن ذلك .
Response: And it is also said to them: If the speech of Allah were created, it would be a body or an attribute of a body. If it were a body, it would be permissible for it to be a speaker, and Allah is able to change both of them. In this is what entails (a consequence) for them, and they must allow that Allah could turn the Qur'an into a human, a jinn, or a devil. Exalted is Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, that His speech should be such. And if it were an attribute of a body like attributes, then Allah is able to make them bodies. So it would be necessary for the Jahmiyyah to allow that Allah could make the Qur'an a corporeal body that eats and drinks, and that He could make it a human and cause it to die. And this is not permissible for the speech of Allah, exalted is He above that.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a second rejoinder that further demonstrates the impossibility of the Qur'an being created by drawing out absurd consequences. The author argues that if the Qur'an were created, it would have to be either a body or an attribute of a body. If it were a body, then it could itself be a speaker (mutakallim), and Allah – being omnipotent – could transform it into another bodily form (like a human, jinn, or devil). Such transformations are obviously impossible for the speech of Allah. If it were an attribute of a body, then Allah could turn that attribute into a body (since He has power over all things), resulting in the Qur'an becoming a physical body that eats and drinks, and even be killed. The Jahmiyyah (the sect holding creationism) are forced to accept these absurdities, but they are clearly impermissible for the eternal speech of Allah. This reductio ad absurdum solidifies the doctrine that the Qur'an is uncreated.

Key Terms
جسم (jism)
نعت لجسم (na't li jism)
الجهمية (al-Jahmiyyah)
مخلوق (makhluq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'attribute of a body' avoids anthropomorphism and thus is a valid option for the created Qur'an.
Correction: The argument shows that even if the Qur'an were an attribute, Allah could turn that attribute into a body, leading to corporeal consequences like eating and dying, which are impossible for the eternal speech of Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the second rejoinder, if the Qur'an were a created body, what would the Jahmiyyah be forced to allow?
A) That the Qur'an could be destroyed by fire.
B) That Allah could turn the Qur'an into a human, jinn, or devil.
C) That the Qur'an could be both body and attribute simultaneously.
D) That the Qur'an is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an cannot be created because that would force absurd corporeal implications for the speech of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you truly feel that you are hearing the uncreated speech of Allah, or does it feel like a mere book from history? What prevents you from experiencing that reality?
?
If you were faced with someone who says the Qur'an is created, are you able to explain the logical absurdities that follow? More importantly, does your heart tremble at the thought of attributing imperfection to Allah's speech?
?
The Jahmiyyah thought they were protecting tawhid by denying the eternity of the Qur'an. Are there any areas in your own faith where you accept a 'compromise' thinking it safeguards Allah's transcendence, but actually it diminishes His majesty? What are they?

Ahmad ibn Hanbal's Categorical Affirmation of the Uncreated Qur'an
Narration of Imam Ahmad affirming the Qur'an is uncreated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal considered the position that the Qur'an is 'neither created nor uncreated' to be more harmful than explicit creationism, and how he used Quranic verses to prove the Qur'an is uncreated.

Core Idea
Denying that the Qur'an is uncreated is worse than saying it is created.

This passage is a historical report from the fifth chapter of al-Ibanah. It records a direct encounter where Imam Ahmad was asked about a new innovation. The questioner presents a group that refuses to take a stand, and Ahmad's response is fierce. He not only affirms the uncreatedness of the Qur'an but also provides a scriptural proof that distinguishes Allah's speech from His creation. This lesson will walk through the narrative and its theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the flow of the story. Notice who is speaking and the context.
This is a direct report from a student of Ahmad.
2
Identify the innovated position
Pay attention to the group described: they say the Qur'an is 'neither created nor uncreated'. Understand why Ahmad calls this more harmful than the Jahmiyyah.
The Jahmiyyah explicitly said the Qur'an is created.
3
Analyze Ahmad's scriptural proof
Focus on the verses Ahmad quotes (7:54 and 55:1-3). See how he distinguishes between 'khalq' (creation) for man and 'ta'lim' (teaching) for the Qur'an.
He repeats the words 'taught' and 'created' to emphasize the distinction.
4
Reflect on the theological conclusion
Ahmad concludes that the Qur'an is from Allah's knowledge. Consider why this means it cannot be created.
Allah's knowledge is an eternal attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الخامس ، ما ذكر من الرواية في القرآن . قال أبو بكر : أتيت أنا والعباس بن عبد العظيم العنبري أبا عبد الله ، فسأل العباس بن عبد العظيم أبا عبد الله أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله ورضي عنه، فقال له: قوم هاهنا قد أحدثوا يقولون : القرآن لا مخلوق ولا غير مخلوق هؤلاء أضر من الجهمية على الناس ويلكم فإن لم تقولوا: ليس بمخلوق فقولوا مخلوق . قال أبو عبد الله : هؤلاء قوم سوء . فقال العباس: ما تقول يا أبا عبد الله؟ فقال : الذي أعتقد وأذهب إليه، ولا أشك فيه، أن القرآن غير مخلوق، ثم قال: سبحان الله شك في هذا؟! ومن ثم تكلم أبو عبد الله مستعظماً للشك في ذلك، فقال: سبحان الله أفي هذا شك؟ قال الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿ أَلَا لَهُ الْخَلْقُ وَالْأَمْرُ ﴾ [الأعراف: ٥٤]. وقال: الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَمَ الْقُرْءَانَ * خَلَقَ الإِنسَانَ ﴾ [الرحمن: ١-٣] ففرق بين الإنسان وبين القرآن، فقال: علم، خلق، فجعل يعيدها: عَلَّمَ، خَلَقَ، أي فَرَّقَ بينهما . قال أبو عبد الله : القرآن [من] علم الله ، ألا تراه يقول : ﴿ عَلَّمَ الْقُرْءَانَ ﴾ .
The fifth chapter: What has been narrated concerning the Qur'an. Abu Bakr said: I and al-‘Abbas ibn ‘Abd al-‘Azim al-‘Anbari came to Abu ‘Abd Allah, and al-‘Abbas ibn ‘Abd al-‘Azim asked Abu ‘Abd Allah Ahmad ibn Hanbal (may Allah have mercy on him and be pleased with him), and said to him: There are people here who have innovated, saying: 'The Qur'an is neither created nor uncreated.' These are more harmful to the people than the Jahmiyyah. Woe to you! If you do not say it is not created, then say it is created. Abu ‘Abd Allah said: These are evil people. Then al-‘Abbas said: What do you say, O Abu ‘Abd Allah? He said: What I believe and hold to, and I have no doubt in it, is that the Qur'an is uncreated. Then he said: Glory be to Allah, is there doubt in this? And then Abu ‘Abd Allah spoke, deeming doubt in that as something grave, and said: Glory be to Allah, is there doubt in this? Allah, Blessed and Exalted, said: 'Indeed, to Him belongs creation and command' (Al-A'raf 54). And He said: 'The Most Merciful taught the Qur'an, created man' (Ar-Rahman 1-3). So He made a distinction between man and the Qur'an: He said 'taught' and 'created'. He kept repeating them: 'taught', 'created' – meaning He differentiated between them. Abu ‘Abd Allah said: The Qur'an is from the knowledge of Allah. Do you not see that He says: 'He taught the Qur'an'?
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a narrated report (riwaya) from Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal that constitutes the fifth chapter. The report begins with Abu Bakr and al-‘Abbas visiting Ahmad. Al-‘Abbas describes a group who have innovated an ambiguous position: they refuse to say the Qur'an is either created or uncreated, which is even more harmful than the Jahmiyya's explicit creationism. Ahmad condemns them as 'evil people'. When asked directly, Ahmad states his unwavering belief: the Qur'an is uncreated (ghayr makhluq). He expresses astonishment that there could be any doubt about this, and he supports his position by quoting two Quranic verses: 'Indeed, to Him belongs creation and command' (7:54) and 'The Most Merciful taught the Qur'an, created man' (55:1-3). Ahmad argues that these verses distinguish between creation (khalq) – referring to man – and the Qur'an, which is described as being taught (ta'lim), not created. Thus the Qur'an is not part of the created order. Furthermore, Ahmad affirms that the Qur'an is from Allah's knowledge ('ilm Allah), pointing to the verse 'He taught the Qur'an' as evidence that it originates from His attribute of knowledge, which is uncreated. The repetition of 'taught' and 'created' emphasizes the fundamental distinction between Allah's speech and created beings.

Key Terms
غير مخلوق (ghayr makhluq)
الجهمية (al-Jahmiyyah)
علم الله ('ilm Allah)
القرآن (al-Qur'an)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that saying the Qur'an is 'neither created nor uncreated' is a safe middle ground that avoids extreme positions.
Correction: Imam Ahmad teaches that this ambiguous position is actually more harmful than the Jahmiyyah's explicit creationism because it introduces doubt and avoids affirming the truth. The Qur'an is clearly uncreated, as proven by the Quranic distinction between creation and teaching.

Checkpoint
What does Ahmad ibn Hanbal use to prove that the Qur'an is uncreated?
A) A hadith from the Prophet.
B) The fact that the Qur'an is miraculous.
C) The Quranic distinction between 'teaching' the Qur'an and 'creating' man.
D) The consensus of the early Muslims.

Key Takeaway
For Ahmad ibn Hanbal, affirming that the Qur'an is uncreated is a non-negotiable belief, and anyone who avoids this affirmation is more dangerous than those who openly deny it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever avoided taking a clear stance on a matter of faith simply to maintain peace or avoid controversy? How does Ahmad ibn Hanbal's passionate condemnation of the 'middle ground' position challenge your own tendency toward comfort and ambiguity? What specific belief will you now affirm more boldly?
?
Ahmad exclaims, 'Glory be to Allah, is there doubt in this?' — examine your own heart: are there any core beliefs about Allah that you treat as optional or tolerate subtle doubts about? What would it cost you to resolve that doubt completely, and what step will you take today to do so?
?
The ambiguous group thought they were being safe, yet Ahmad called them more harmful than the Jahmiyyah. Is there any area of your life — not just theology but action — where you are taking a 'middle ground' that actually denies the truth? What is the specific change you will make this week to align fully with what you know is right?

Waki's Ruling on the Createdness of the Qur'an
Narration of Waki' stating the ruling on the creator of the Qur'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early Sunni position that declaring the Qur'an created constitutes apostasy, and the legal procedure of istitaba that follows.

Core Idea
Saying the Qur'an is created was considered apostasy by early scholars.

This lesson presents a direct legal ruling from the early scholar Waki' ibn al-Jarrah. The statement is brief but carries immense weight, showing that the issue of the Qur'an's createdness was not a mere theological nuance but a boundary marker of orthodoxy. Waki' makes clear that holding this view places one outside the fold of Islam, subject to the same consequences as apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the concise legal language used by Waki'.
2
Identify key terms
Find the words for 'apostate' (مُرْتَد), 'asked to repent' (يُسْتَتَاب), and 'killed' (يُقْتَل). These define the ruling.
3
Understand the procedure
Note that the person is not immediately executed but given a chance to repent (istitaba). This reflects Islamic legal principles.
Repentance means renouncing the belief that the Qur'an is created.
4
Reflect on the gravity
Consider why the createdness of the Qur'an was considered a foundational issue. Early Sunnis saw it as a direct challenge to Allah's eternal speech.
5
Apply the lesson
Ask yourself: How does this ruling help define Sunni identity against Mu'tazilite thought?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الحسين بن عبد الأول، قال: سمعت وكيعاً يقول : من قال: القرآن مخلوق فهو مرتد يستتاب فإن تاب وإلا قتل .
And Al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Awwal mentioned, he said: I heard Waki' saying: Whoever says the Qur'an is created, he is an apostate; he is asked to repent; if he repents (well and good), otherwise he is killed.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a brief legal ruling (fatwa) from the early scholar Waki' ibn al-Jarrah (d. 196/812). He states that the one who claims the Qur'an is created commits apostasy (ridda). The ruling includes a procedure: the person is first given the opportunity to repent (istitaba). If he repents, he is left alone; if he refuses, he is executed. This reflects the view among early Sunni scholars that the createdness of the Qur'an was a grave heresy equivalent to leaving Islam.

Key Terms
مرتد
يستتاب
يقتل
القرآن مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that saying the Qur'an is created is a minor theological opinion with no legal consequences.
Correction: This narration shows that it was considered apostasy, subjecting the person to the death penalty if unrepentant.

Checkpoint

D) He should be flogged

Key Takeaway
Waki' declares that asserting the Qur'an is created constitutes apostasy, carrying the penalty of death if unrepented.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Ibn al-Mubarak on the Danger of Describing Jahmiyya
Ibn al-Mubarak's statement on the extreme deviance of Jahmiyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extreme caution early Sunni scholars exercised regarding the Jahmiyya sect, to the extent that even describing their speech was considered dangerous.

Core Idea
Some deviance is so extreme that even describing it risks disbelief.

Imam al-Ash'ari records a powerful statement from Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, a revered early scholar, comparing the speech of Jews and Christians with that of the Jahmiyya. Ibn al-Mubarak's reluctance to even repeat their words reveals the depth of their deviation. The narrator adds a sobering reflection: engaging with such ideas might lead one into unbelief unknowingly.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the chain of transmission and the two parts: Ibn al-Mubarak's statement and the narrator's comment.
2
Contrast the three groups
Ibn al-Mubarak contrasts Jahmiyya with Jews and Christians. He can describe the speech of Jews and Christians but not of Jahmiyya. Why do you think that is?
Consider the severity of the deviation.
3
Reflect on the narrator's warning
The narrator, Muhammad, says: 'We fear that we may disbelieve while we do not know.' What does this reveal about the danger of engaging with Jahmiyya ideas?
This shows concern that one might inadvertently fall into disbelief.
4
Apply the lesson
Think about how this caution applies to dealing with extreme deviant groups today. Should we be similarly careful?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر محمد بن الصباح البزار قال حدثنا علي بن الحسن بن شقيق قال سمعت ابن المبارك يقول : إنا نستطيع أن نحكي كلام اليهود والنصارى ولا نستطيع أن نحكي كلام الجهمية. قال محمد: نقول : نخاف أن نكفر ولا نعلم .
And Muhammad ibn al-Sabbah al-Bazzar mentioned, he said: Ali ibn al-Hasan ibn Shuqayq narrated to us, he said: I heard Ibn al-Mubarak saying: We are able to relate the speech of the Jews and Christians, but we are not able to relate the speech of the Jahmiyya. Muhammad said: We say: We fear that we may disbelieve while we do not know.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage reports a statement by the renowned scholar Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak (d. 181/797) comparing the speech of Jews and Christians with that of the Jahmiyya (a sect associated with Jahm ibn Safwan, often accused of extreme anthropomorphism denial and other heresies). Ibn al-Mubarak asserts that he can recount the statements of Jews and Christians (which he considers false but describable), but he cannot even describe the speech of the Jahmiyya because it is so repugnant or dangerous. The narrator Muhammad (likely al-Bazzar) adds a comment: 'We fear that we may disbelieve while we do not know,' indicating that engaging with Jahmiyya ideas might inadvertently lead one into disbelief without realizing it. This highlights the extreme caution early scholars exercised regarding this sect.

Key Terms

يهود

نخاف أن نكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage is about the createdness of the Qur'an.
Correction: The passage is about the difficulty of even describing Jahmiyya views, not specifically about the createdness of the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Mubarak's reluctance to even describe Jahmiyya speech demonstrates the extreme caution early Sunni scholars took to avoid any proximity to disbelief.

Hammad's Declaration of Innocence from Abu Hanifa
Report of Hammad's dissociation from Abu Hanifa over the created Qur'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical report of Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman declaring himself free from Abu Hanifa due to Abu Hanifa's belief in the createdness of the Qur'an, and the significance of the term 'mushrik' in this context.

Core Idea
For some early traditionists, belief in a created Qur'an was tantamount to polytheism.

This passage from al-Ibanah reports a dramatic exchange between two early scholars. Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman instructs Sufyan al-Thawri to convey a harsh message to Abu Hanifa, calling him a polytheist and declaring dissociation. The reason given is Abu Hanifa's stance on the Qur'an. This illustrates how seriously the early Ahl al-Hadith took the issue of the createdness of the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the report carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Note the chain of narrators and the core message.
The chain is long: Harun -> Abu Nu'aym -> Sulayman -> Sufyan -> Hammad.
2
Identify the key figures
Identify Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, Sufyan al-Thawri, and Abu Hanifa. What is their scholarly relationship? Hammad was Sufyan's teacher; Abu Hanifa was a contemporary.
3
Analyze the strong language
Notice the words 'al-mushrik' (the polytheist) and 'bari'' (innocent/dissociated). Why would Hammad use such intense terms? Consider the theological stakes.
This reflects the high tension over the created Qur'an.
4
Connect to the broader controversy
The createdness of the Qur'an was a major test of orthodoxy. This report shows a hardline condemnation. Reflect on how al-Ash'ari uses this to support his own position.
Al-Ash'ari likely includes this to show precedent for condemning the view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر هارون بن إسحاق الهمداني عن أبي نعيم، عن سليمان بن عيسى القاري عن سفيان الثوري قال: قال لي حماد بن أبي سليمان: بلغ أبا حنيفة المشرك أني منه بريء قال سليمان ثم قال سفيان؛ لأنه كان يقول القرآن مخلوق
And Harun ibn Ishaq al-Hamadani mentioned, from Abu Nu'aym, from Sulayman ibn Isa al-Qari, from Sufyan al-Thawri, he said: Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman said to me: Inform Abu Hanifa the polytheist that I am free from him. Sulayman said: Then Sufyan said: Because he used to say the Qur'an is created.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage reports a chain of transmission leading to Sufyan al-Thawri (d. 161/778). Sufyan recounts that Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman (his teacher, d. 120/737) instructed him to convey a message to Abu Hanifa (d. 150/767), calling him 'the polytheist' (al-mushrik) and declaring himself innocent of him. The reason given is that Abu Hanifa held the view that the Qur'an is created. This reflects the intense hostility among some early traditionists towards Abu Hanifa on this theological point. The use of the term 'mushrik' is strong and shows that these scholars equated the belief in a created Qur'an with associating partners with Allah.

Key Terms
أبو حنيفة
المشرك
بريء
القرآن مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Abu Hanifa was universally respected and that this report is exceptional or inconsequential.
Correction: The report shows that some early authorities like Hammad and Sufyan considered Abu Hanifa's view on the Qur'an so serious that they called him a polytheist and dissociated from him.

Checkpoint
Why did Hammad declare himself free from Abu Hanifa?
A) Because Abu Hanifa held heretical views on predestination
B) Because Abu Hanifa said the Qur'an is created
C) Because Abu Hanifa associated partners with Allah
D) Because Abu Hanifa opposed the Sunnah

Key Takeaway
This report shows that for some early scholars, belief in a created Qur'an was considered sufficient for dissociation and labeling someone a polytheist.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you knew someone held a belief that you considered tantamount to shirk, would you have the courage to declare yourself free from them, as Hammad did? Why or why not?
?
What are some beliefs today that you might be tempted to overlook for the sake of unity? How does this lesson challenge you to reconsider that tolerance?
?
Imagine you are in the position of Sufyan, tasked with conveying a harsh truth. Would you deliver the message faithfully or soften it? What does your answer reveal about your commitment to truth over relationships?

Abu Hanifa's Repentance from the Createdness of the Qur'an
Report that Abu Hanifa repented from the view that the Qur'an is created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the report that Abu Hanifa repented from the view that the Qur'an is created and the significance of this narration in the historical debate.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa reportedly repented, but the text breaks off before giving his reason.

This lesson presents a key historical report from the grandson of Abu Hanifa, stating that the great Imam was asked to repent from saying the Qur'an is created. According to the narration, he did repent and announced it publicly. However, the text ends abruptly, leaving his exact reason unclear. This report is often cited in theological debates about the createdness of the Qur'an and the stance of early scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice that it is a chain of narration from Sufyan ibn Waki' to Umar ibn Hammad to his father. The text ends mid-sentence.
The passage has high OCR risk; some words may be unclear.
2
Analyze the content
Identify the key claim: Abu Hanifa repented from saying the Qur'an is created. Note the witness: his son Hammad informs the grandson.
3
Consider the missing ending
The narration breaks off at 'I feared, by Allah, that...' Reflect on what Abu Hanifa might have feared (e.g., disbelief, punishment).
The commentary speculates that he feared being a disbeliever.
4
Evaluate the report's significance
This report is used to argue that even Abu Hanifa eventually recanted his view. However, its authenticity is questioned. Consider how missing text affects interpretation.
This connects to the broader historical debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Abu Hanifa did repent and then went around (presumably informing others) of his repentance. When asked why he changed his view, Abu Hanifa began to answer: 'I feared, by Allah, that...' but the text breaks off. The implied completion would be something like 'I feared that I would be a disbeliever' or 'I feared Allah's punishment.' This narration is important because it suggests that even Abu Hanifa, initially known for this view, recanted. However, the authenticity of this report may be questioned, and the missing ending leaves some ambiguity.

Ibn al-Mubarak on the Difficulty of Refuting the Jahmiyya
Ibn al-Mubarak says the Jahmiyya are harder to refute than Jews and Christians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ibn al-Mubarak considered the Jahmiyya more dangerous than Jews and Christians, and the importance of cautious engagement with theological innovation.

Core Idea
The Jahmiyya are more difficult to refute than Jews and Christians because their arguments are subtle and lead to disbelief.

This short narration from the early scholar 'Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak offers a striking insight into the early Muslim encounter with deviant theological movements. Ibn al-Mubarak compares the relative ease of refuting well-known religions to the difficulty of even recounting the words of the Jahmiyya, a sect that denied Allah's attributes. His warning is not just about argumentation—it is about the risk of falling into disbelief without realizing it. Let's examine the passage carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the chain of narration and the key terms used.
The chain (isnad) shows the reliability of the report.
2
Understand 'حكي الكلام'
The phrase 'نحكي كلام' means 'to reproduce or recount speech' – implying the ability to quote and refute arguments. Ibn al-Mubarak says they can do this for Jews and Christians but not for the Jahmiyya.
This highlights the subtlety and confusion caused by Jahmi arguments.
3
Reflect on the fear of disbelief
The narrator adds: 'We fear that we may disbelieve and we do not know.' This shows the danger of engaging with such ideas without proper knowledge.
The fear is not that the Jahmiyya are disbelievers, but that one might be misled into disbelief.
4
Apply the lesson today
Consider how this principle applies to modern deviant sects or ideologies. How should a Muslim approach arguments that are confusing or subversive?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر محمد بن الصباح البزار قال حدثنا علي بن الحسن بن شقيق قال سمعت ابن المبارك يقول : إنا نستطيع أن نحكي كلام اليهود والنصارى ولا نستطيع أن نحكي كلام الجهمية. قال محمد: نقول : نخاف أن نكفر ولا نعلم .
And Muhammad ibn al-Sabah al-Bazzar mentioned, he said: 'Ali ibn al-Hasan ibn Shaqiq narrated to us, he said: I heard Ibn al-Mubarak saying: Verily we are able to reproduce the speech of the Jews and Christians, but we are not able to reproduce the speech of the Jahmiyya. Muhammad said: We say: We fear that we may disbelieve and we do not know.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage contains two statements. First, Ibn al-Mubarak (the famous scholar) makes an observation about the Jahmiyya, a sect that denied the attributes of Allah. He says that Muslims can quote and refute the arguments of Jews and Christians, but they cannot even properly recount (haki) the speech of the Jahmiyya because it is so deviant and difficult to pin down. Then the narrator or compiler Muhammad (likely Imam al-Ash'ari himself, as he often says 'qala Muhammad') adds a comment: 'We say: We fear that we may disbelieve and we do not know.' This expresses a cautious attitude: due to the confusion caused by the Jahmiyya's arguments, some people might fall into disbelief unknowingly. It highlights the danger of engaging with such deviant ideas without solid knowledge.

Key Terms
الجهمية
حكي الكلام
خوف الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ibn al-Mubarak is declaring the Jahmiyya as disbelievers.
Correction: He is not making a takfir; rather, he is warning that engaging with their arguments can inadvertently lead to disbelief due to their subtlety. The fear is for the listener, not necessarily a judgment on the Jahmiyya themselves.

Checkpoint
What did Ibn al-Mubarak say about the speech of the Jahmiyya?
A) It is easy to refute
B) It is harder to refute than the speech of Jews and Christians
C) It is the same as the speech of Jews and Christians
D) It is not worth engaging with

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Mubarak warns that the Jahmiyya are more dangerous than Jews and Christians because their subtle arguments can lead to disbelief without the person realizing it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you engaged in a theological debate without full certainty of your own understanding? Are you willing to remain silent rather than risk speaking in a way that could damage your faith?
?
Ibn al-Mubarak feared disbelieving without knowing. If you were exposed to a subtle heretical argument today, would you recognize it, or would it slip into your heart? What will you do to strengthen your immunity?

Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman Disassociates from Abu Hanifa
Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman declares disassociation from Abu Hanifa due to his view on the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how serious the issue of the created Quran was among early Sunnis, as seen in Hammad's strong response to Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Calling the Quran created was considered shirk by early Sunni scholars.

This lesson presents a stark historical report from early Islamic history. Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, a teacher of Abu Hanifa, instructed Sufyan al-Thawri to inform Abu Hanifa that he disassociates from him, calling him a mushrik, solely because Abu Hanifa held that the Quran is created. This reveals the intensity of early debates over the nature of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration and note the chain
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the chain of narrators (isnad). Write down the names in order.
The chain is: Harun ibn Ishaq al-Hamdani → Abu Nu'aym → Sulayman ibn 'Isa al-Qari → Sufyan al-Thawri → Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman.
2
Understand the doctrinal issue
Identify the core belief that caused the disassociation: Abu Hanifa's statement that 'the Quran is created.' Reflect on why this was considered so grave by Hammad.
In Sunni orthodoxy, the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah. Calling it created was seen as diminishing Allah's attributes.
3
Reflect on the implications and context
Consider why Hammad used the term 'mushrik' and whether this report alone gives the full picture. Then think about the need to see later reports of Abu Hanifa's repentance.
This report must be read alongside other narrations that show Abu Hanifa retracted this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر هارون بن إسحاق الهمداني عن أبي نعيم، عن سليمان بن عيسى القاري عن سفيان الثوري قال: قال لي حماد بن أبي سليمان: بلغ أبا حنيفة المشرك أني منه بريء. قال سليمان ثم قال سفيان؛ لأنه كان يقول القرآن مخلوق
And Harun ibn Ishaq al-Hamdani mentioned, from Abu Nu'aym, from Sulayman ibn 'Isa al-Qari, from Sufyan al-Thawri, he said: Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman said to me: Inform Abu Hanifa the mushrik that I am free of him. Sulayman said, then Sufyan said: Because he used to say the Quran is created.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This is a report from Sufyan al-Thawri that Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman instructed him to tell Abu Hanifa that he (Hammad) disassociates himself from Abu Hanifa due to Abu Hanifa's statement that the Quran is created. The harsh language 'al-mushrik' (the polytheist) indicates that Hammad considered this belief tantamount to shirk. This shows the severity of the issue among the early scholars, though later scholars clarified that Abu Hanifa repented from this view, as seen in subsequent reports.

Key Terms
براءة
مشرك
خلق القرآن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Hanifa died upon the belief that the Quran is created.
Correction: Later reports in the same source show that Abu Hanifa repented from this view before his death.

Checkpoint

A) Because Abu Hanifa was a polytheist
B) Because Abu Hanifa said the Quran is created
C) Because Abu Hanifa disagreed with him on a different issue
D) Because Abu Hanifa was Qadari

Key Takeaway
This report illustrates the severity of the created Quran controversy but must be read alongside Abu Hanifa's repentance narration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This report shows that even respected scholars like Hammad could err in judgment if they didn't wait for the full picture. Where in your life are you judging someone prematurely? Will you seek the full truth and give them the benefit of the doubt?

Abu Hanifa's Repentance: Taqiyya Under Duress
A report on Abu Hanifa's repentance and his admission of taqiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical report of Abu Hanifa's repentance from the statement that the Quran is created and the role of taqiyya in his decision.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa's repentance was an act of taqiyya, not a change in belief.

This lesson examines a critical historical report about Imam Abu Hanifa. According to the narration, he was forced to repent from saying the Quran is created. When questioned, he admitted he acted out of fear, raising important questions about the use of taqiyya (dissimulation) under duress and the political pressures early Sunni scholars faced.

Guided Path
1
Read the report carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the chain of narration and the key figures: Sufyan ibn Waki', 'Umar ibn Hammad, and Abu Hanifa's son Hammad.
The chain includes three narrators before reaching Abu Hanifa.
2
Identify the event and context
Ibn Abi Layla demanded repentance from Abu Hanifa for his statement that the Quran is created. Understand that this was a controversial theological position at the time.
Ibn Abi Layla was a judge with authority to enforce orthodoxy.
3
Analyze the motive for repentance
Abu Hanifa explicitly states he repented out of fear, not conviction. He calls it taqiyya. Consider what taqiyya means and when it is permissible.
Taqiyya is allowing dissimulation to protect oneself from harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر سفيان بن وكيع قال سمعت عمر بن حماد بن أبي حنيفة قال : أخبرني أبي قال: الكلام الذي استتاب منه ابن أبي ليلى أبا حنيفة هو قوله : القرآن مخلوق قال فتاب منه وطاف به في الخلق، قال أبي : فقلت له : كيف صرت إلى هذا؟ قال: خفت والله أن يقدم علي فأعطيته التقية
And Sufyan ibn Waki' mentioned, he said: I heard 'Umar ibn Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa say: My father informed me: The statement for which Ibn Abi Layla asked Abu Hanifa to repent was his saying: The Quran is created. He said: So he repented from it and went around among the people [announcing it]. My father said: I said to him: How did you come to this? He said: I feared, by Allah, that he would proceed against me, so I gave him taqiyya (dissimulation).
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage recounts the repentance of Abu Hanifa from the view that the Quran is created. The report comes from his grandson 'Umar ibn Hammad via his father. The judge Ibn Abi Layla demanded that Abu Hanifa repent from this statement. Abu Hanifa did repent and publicly announced it. When asked why he repented, he admitted it was out of fear of punishment (taqiyya), not necessarily because he changed his belief. This raises issues of taqiyya under duress. The report shows that even the great imam was pressured on this issue.

Key Terms
توبة
تقية
خلق القرآن
استتابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Hanifa never held the view that the Quran is created.
Correction: This report indicates that he did hold that view at one point, but later recanted under duress.

Checkpoint

A) He was convinced by arguments
B) He feared the authorities
C) He wanted to avoid fitna
D) He never actually repented

Key Takeaway
This report illustrates the use of taqiyya under duress and the historical pressures on early scholars regarding the createdness of the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you outwardly conformed to a belief or practice you don't hold to avoid conflict or harm? How did that affect your relationship with Allah? What will you do the next time you face such pressure?
?
Is there a conviction about your faith that you are afraid to voice in public? What is the worst that could happen? How can you prepare yourself to stand firm even at personal cost?
?
Abu Hanifa chose taqiyya to save his life. What would you be willing to sacrifice—comfort, reputation, relationships—rather than compromise your creed? What step will you take today to strengthen that resolve?

Hammad's Demand for Repentance from Abu Hanifa
Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman sends a message to Abu Hanifa demanding repentance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second report of Hammad disassociating from Abu Hanifa and the implication of Abu Hanifa's alleged relapse.

Core Idea
A teacher's demand for repentance reveals the seriousness of doctrinal deviation.

This brief narration from the early Muslim community adds another layer to the controversy surrounding Abu Hanifa's theological stance. Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, Abu Hanifa's own teacher, not only disassociates from him but also sends a message with an ultimatum. Furthermore, an accusation suggests that Abu Hanifa may have reverted after initially repenting. This passage highlights the intense scrutiny and communal sanctions faced by those accused of innovation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the chain of transmission and the key actions.
The passage is a short report, so pay attention to each detail.
2
Identify the main claims
Identify the two main parts: Hammad's message to Abu Hanifa and the additional testimony about a relapse. Note the condition of repentance.
The condition 'unless you repent' is crucial.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why Hammad, as a teacher, would disassociate from Abu Hanifa and demand repentance. What does this tell us about the gravity of theological disagreement?
This episode shows the high stakes of 'ilm al-kalam disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Abu Hanifa's Retraction from the Created Quran
Abu Yusuf reports debating Abu Hanifa for two months until he retracted from the createdness of the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the report of Abu Yusuf is significant in establishing the correct Sunni view on the createdness of the Quran and how it clarifies the stance of Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf's report shows that Abu Hanifa ultimately rejected the createdness of the Quran.

The issue of whether the Quran is created or uncreated was a major point of contention in early Islamic theology. While some attributed the view that the Quran is created to Abu Hanifa, the testimony of his own student, Abu Yusuf, provides direct evidence that Abu Hanifa retracted that position after a lengthy debate. In this lesson, we examine this critical report.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and Translation
Read the short Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the key verbs: ناظر (debated) and رجع (retracted).
2
Understand the Theological Context
Recall that the createdness of the Quran was a divisive issue. Some groups, like the Mu'tazila, held that the Quran is created, while the Sunni position is that it is uncreated and eternal.
3
Analyze the Significance of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf was a close student of Abu Hanifa and a renowned jurist. His firsthand account carries weight as an eyewitness to Abu Hanifa's final position.
The report indicates a two-month debate, showing serious engagement.
4
Address the Common Misunderstanding
Some claim Abu Hanifa never changed his view. This report directly contradicts that claim, as it explicitly states that he retracted.
5
Summarize the Lesson
Reflect on how this short report reinforces the Sunni belief in the uncreated Quran and clarifies the stance of a major early scholar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذُكر عن أبي يوسف قال: ناظرت أبا حنيفة شهرين حتى رجع عن خلق القرآن .
And it was mentioned from Abu Yusuf that he said: I debated Abu Hanifa for two months until he retracted from [the belief in] the createdness of the Quran.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This short report from Abu Yusuf (the famous Hanafi jurist and student of Abu Hanifa) states that he engaged in a lengthy debate with his teacher over the issue of the createdness of the Quran, and after two months Abu Hanifa retracted his view. This emphasizes that the position of the created Quran was not the final view of Abu Hanifa, as he eventually abandoned it.

Key Terms
ناظر
رجع
خلق القرآن
أبو حنيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim Abu Hanifa never changed his view on the createdness of the Quran.
Correction: This report directly contradicts that, as Abu Yusuf states that Abu Hanifa retracted after a two-month debate.

Checkpoint

A) Two weeks
B) Two months
C) Two years
D) One month

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa retracted the view of the createdness of the Quran after a two-month debate with his student Abu Yusuf.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you been confronted with evidence that you were wrong about a deeply held belief? Did you retract with humility, or did you resist? What would it take for you to change your mind today?
?
Abu Yusuf spent two months debating his own teacher. Is there a truth you are avoiding because it would mean challenging someone you respect? Will you seek it anyway?
?
Retracting a view can be humiliating. Have you ever had to admit a mistake in front of others? What held you back? This lesson reminds us that even great scholars changed their positions. Are you clinging to an idea out of pride rather than evidence?

Abu Hanifa's Recantation from Khalq al-Qur'an
Al-Ash'ari narrates two reports of Abu Hanifa's recantation from the createdness of the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical evidence that Abu Hanifa recanted from the createdness of the Quran, as reported by Imam al-Ash'ari in al-Ibanah.

Core Idea
Two narrations confirm Abu Hanifa's repentance from the view that the Quran is created.

Imam al-Ash'ari, in defending the orthodox Sunni position that the Quran is uncreated, presents historical reports that even the great imam Abu Hanifa ultimately recanted from the Mu'tazili doctrine of the created Quran. This lesson examines two such narrations, one from Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman and another from Abu Yusuf, which together build a case that the early Hanafi school rejected khalq al-Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the full narration carefully. Notice that it contains two separate reports, each with its own chain of transmission. Pay attention to the names mentioned.
2
Analyze the first narration
Identify the key elements: Hammad's message demanding repentance, and the claim that Abu Hanifa later invited someone to the same position he had repented from. What does this suggest about his final stance?
3
Analyze the second narration
Abu Yusuf, a prominent student of Abu Hanifa, states he debated him for two months until he recanted. Why is Abu Yusuf's testimony particularly significant for establishing Abu Hanifa's final position?

وذكر هارون بن إسحاق قال: سمعت إسماعيل بن أبي الحكم يذكر عن عمر بن عبيد الطنافسي؛ أن حماد بن أبي سليمان بحث إلى أبي حنيفة: إني بريء مما تقول إلا أن تتوب وكان عنده ابن أبي غنية، قال: فقال: أخبرني جارك أن أبا حنيفة دعاه إلى ما استتيب منه بعد ما استتيب. وذُكر عن أبي يوسف قال: ناظرت أبا حنيفة شهرين حتى رجع عن خلق القرآن.
And Harun ibn Ishaq mentioned, he said: I heard Isma'il ibn Abi al-Hakam mention on the authority of 'Umar ibn 'Ubayd al-Tanafisi: That Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman sent a message to Abu Hanifa: 'I am innocent of what you say unless you repent' – and Ibn Abi Ghaniya was with him. He said: He said: 'Your neighbor told me that Abu Hanifa invited him to what he was asked to repent from after he had been asked to repent.' And it was mentioned from Abu Yusuf, he said: I debated Abu Hanifa for two months until he recanted from the createdness of the Quran.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage reports two narrations concerning Abu Hanifa's position on the createdness of the Quran. The first narration involves Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman declaring his innocence of Abu Hanifa's view unless he repents, and a witness claiming Abu Hanifa called someone to a position from which he later repented. The second narration from Abu Yusuf states that after two months of debate, Abu Hanifa recanted from the belief that the Quran is created. These reports serve as historical evidence that the early Hanafi school did not hold to the doctrine of the created Quran, and that Abu Hanifa himself ultimately rejected it.

B) Two months

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari provides historical evidence that Abu Hanifa recanted from the createdness of the Quran, thereby aligning the Hanafi school with orthodox Sunni belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refuting the Waqfiyya: The Logical Inconsistency of Suspension
Imam Ashari refutes the position of tawaqquf by dialectical argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dialectical argument Imam Ashari uses to refute the position of tawaqquf, showing that suspending judgment on the Quran's nature is logically self-defeating.

Core Idea
Suspending judgment requires evidence, and the waqfiyya have none.

Imam Ashari now confronts a third position: those who neither affirm that the Quran is created nor uncreated, but pause (waqf). This might seem like a cautious middle ground, but Ashari's razor-sharp dialectic shows it is actually an unstable position. He forces the waqfiyya to apply their own principle consistently, and they collapse into contradiction. Read carefully as Ashari turns their own argument against them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Notice the back-and-forth structure: the waqfiyya's claim, their justification, and Ashari's counter-questions.
Pay attention to the word 'وقف' (waqf) and its derivatives.
2
Identify the waqfiyya's argument
The waqfiyya claim that because no explicit text states the Quran is created or uncreated, they suspend judgment. Note their reliance on absence of evidence.
They say: 'Allah did not say... nor did the Messenger... nor did the Muslims agree.'
3
Follow Ashari's first counter
Ashari asks: is there any text commanding you to stop? If they claim yes, they lie. If they say no, then by their own logic they should not stop, because there is also no text commanding stop.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: their principle leads to the opposite conclusion.
4
Understand the second counter
Ashari then asks why they deny evidence that the Quran is uncreated. They merely say 'we did not find it.' This shows their position is based on ignorance, not knowledge.
The burden of proof is on them to show absence of evidence, not just claim it.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why tawaqquf is not a safe middle ground. The Quran's nature is either created or uncreated; avoiding the question does not solve the issue.
Aqeedah demands certainty, not suspension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب السادس
الكلام على من وقف في القرآن وقال :
لا أقول إنه مخلوق ولا أقول إنه غير مخلوق

١٣٢- جواب :
يقال لهم : لم زعمتم ذلك وقلتموه؟ فإن قالوا: قلنا ذلك ؛ لأن الله لم يقل في كتابه: إنه مخلوق، ولا قاله رسول الله ، ولا أجمـع عـلـيـه المسلمون، ولم يقل في كتابه إنه غير مخلوق ولا قال ذلك رسول الله ، ولا أجمع عليه المسلمون فوقفنا لذلك، ولم نقل إنه مخلوق، ولا إنه غير مخلوق .
يقال لهم : فهل قال الله عز وجل لكم في كتابه قفوا فيه ولا تقولوا إنـه غير مخلوق، وهل قال لكم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم توقفوا عن أن تقولوا إنه غير مخلوق، وهل أجمع المسلمون على التوقف عن القول إنه غير مخلوق؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، فقد بهتوا .
وإن قالوا: لا، قيل لهم : فلا تقفوا عن أن تقولوا غير مخلوق بمثل الحجة التي بها ألزمتم أنفسكم التوقف .
ثم يقال لهم: ولم أبيتم أن يكون في كتاب الله ما يدل على أن القرآن
غير مخلوق؟
فإن قالوا: لم نجده .
Chapter Six
Discussion on those who stop regarding the Quran and say:
I do not say it is created nor do I say it is uncreated.

132- Answer:
It is said to them: Why did you claim that and say it? If they say: We said that because Allah did not say in His Book that it is created, nor did His Messenger say it, nor did the Muslims agree upon it, and He did not say in His Book that it is uncreated, nor did His Messenger say that, nor did the Muslims agree upon it, so we stopped for that reason, and we do not say it is created nor that it is uncreated.
It is said to them: Did Allah, mighty and majestic, say to you in His Book to stop over it and not say it is uncreated, and did His Messenger, peace be upon him, say to you to stop from saying it is uncreated, and did the Muslims agree upon stopping from saying it is uncreated? If they say: Yes, then they have lied.
And if they say: No, then it is said to them: Then do not stop from saying it is uncreated based on the same proof by which you obliged yourselves to stop.
Then it is said to them: Why do you refuse that in the Book of Allah there is evidence that the Quran is uncreated?
If they say: We did not find it.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the position of tawaqquf (suspension of judgment) regarding the Quran. Imam Ashari presents a dialectical argument. He first asks the waqfiyya why they pause. Their answer: because there is no explicit text stating the Quran is created or uncreated. Then Ashari turns their argument against them: Is there any text commanding you to stop? If they claim yes, they are lying. If they admit no, then by their own principle (absence of text justifies pause), they should not pause, because there is no text commanding pause either. He then asks why they deny that the Quran contains evidence for its uncreatedness; they merely say they did not find it. This exposes the weakness of their position: they rely on a lack of explicit proof for both sides, but they have no basis to reject the proof that exists. The argument is a classic reductio ad absurdum.

Key Terms
وقف
مخلوق
غير مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that suspending judgment on the Quran's nature (waqf) is a safe, neutral position that avoids extremes.
Correction: Ashari demonstrates that waqf is not neutral; it is itself a position that requires evidence. The waqfiyya cannot justify their pause without contradicting their own principle. Aqeedah demands clarity, not suspension.

Checkpoint
What is the argument of those who pause (waqfiyya) for not saying the Quran is uncreated?
A) They believe it is created
B) They believe it is uncreated
C) They find no explicit text either way
D) They follow al-Ash'ari

Key Takeaway
Suspending judgment on the Quran's nature is not a safe middle ground but a logically inconsistent position that requires evidence just like any other claim.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever stayed silent on a matter of truth to avoid conflict or accusation? How did your silence actually become a claim that demanded evidence — and did you have any?
?
When you say 'I don't know' about an important theological matter, are you genuinely seeking, or are you using ignorance as a comfortable shield? The Waqfiyya were asked: 'Why do you refuse to see the evidence?' What evidence about Allah's speech are you avoiding in your own heart?
?
Imam Ashari exposes that suspending judgment is not a neutral safe zone — it's a position that requires proof just like any other. Is there an area of your faith where you have paused, not out of humility, but out of fear of commitment? What would it cost you to take a definitive stance on the uncreatedness of the Quran?

The Claim and Its First Absurdity
Al-Ash'ari states the Mu'tazila claim and its first absurd implication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the absurd consequence of the Mu'tazila claim that Allah is everywhere.

Core Idea
If Allah is everywhere, He would be in the most unclean places.

Al-Ash'ari begins his refutation by stating the position of the Mu'tazila and their allies. He immediately points out a logical consequence that is offensive to religious sensibility. This lesson examines that first argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim
Read the Arabic line where al-Ash'ari reports the belief of the Mu'tazila, Haruriyya, and Jahmiyya that Allah is in every place.
Notice that he groups three sects together.
2
Identify the consequence
Find the word 'فلزمهم' (so it necessarily follows) and see what consequence he draws.
3
Consider the absurdity
Reflect on why mentioning the womb of Mary and latrines is a powerful rhetorical move.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
Understand the conclusion
Read how al-Ash'ari concludes this part: 'وهذا خلاف الدين' – this is contrary to the religion.
He doesn't just say it's illogical; it's against the religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعمت المعتزلة والحرورية والجهمية أن الله عز وجل في كل مكان فلزمهم أنه في بطن مريم وفي الحشوش والأخلية، وهذا خلاف الدين، تعالى الله عن قولهم علواً كبيراً.
جواب :
ويقال لهم : إذا لم يكن مستوياً على العرش بمعنى يختص العرش دون غيره كما قال ذلك أهل العلم ونقلة الآثار وحملة الأخبار، وكان الله عز وجل في كل مكان، فهو تحت الأرض التي السماء فوقها، وإذا كان تحت الأرض والأرض فوقه، والسماء فوق الأرض، ففي هذا ما يلزمكم أن تقولوا : إن الله تحت التحت والأشياء فوقه، وأنه فوق الفوق والأشياء تحته، وفي هذا ما يجب أنه تحت ما هو فوقه وفوق ما هو تحته، وهذا هو المحال المتناقض، تعالى الله عن افترائكم عليه علواً كبيراً.
The Mu'tazila, Haruriyya, and Jahmiyya claimed that Allah Almighty is in every place, so it necessarily follows that He is in the womb of Mary and in latrines and cesspits, and this is contrary to the religion. Exalted is Allah above their saying, greatly exalted.
Answer:
It is said to them: If He is not established on the Throne (mustawiyan 'ala al-'arsh) in a sense that distinguishes the Throne from other places, as the people of knowledge, transmitters of traditions, and bearers of reports say, and Allah is in every place, then He is under the earth which the sky is above. If He is under the earth and the earth is above Him, and the sky is above the earth, then this necessitates that you say: Allah is under the underneath and things are above Him, and that He is above the above and things are underneath Him, and this necessitates that He is under what is above Him and above what is underneath Him. This is impossible contradiction. Exalted is Allah above your falsehood against Him, greatly exalted.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Allah is everywhere. Al-Ash'ari first states the position of the Mu'tazila, Haruriyya (Kharijites), and Jahmiyya, who assert that Allah is in every place. He argues that this logically implies Allah would be in impure places like the womb of Mary and latrines, which is contrary to religious decency. Then he presents a reductio ad absurdum: if Allah is not specifically established on the Throne (istiwa') as the orthodox scholars hold, and He is everywhere, then He would be under the earth (since the sky is above the earth), leading to the contradictory situation of being both above and below simultaneously. This demonstrates the impossibility of the claim, and he concludes by declaring Allah exalted above their falsehood.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الحرورية
الجهمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah being omnipresent means He is physically located in every place, including impure places.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that such a belief leads to absurd and irreligious conclusions; divine omnipresence should be understood differently (as knowledge and power).

Checkpoint
Which groups does al-Ash'ari mention as holding that Allah is everywhere?
A) Mu'tazila and Ash'aris
B) Mu'tazila, Haruriyya, and Jahmiyya
C) Haruriyya and Qadariyya
D) Jahmiyya and Murji'a

Key Takeaway
The claim that Allah is everywhere in a literal sense leads to absurd consequences that contradict religious decency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever casually thought of Allah as 'everywhere' without considering the implications? How does this passage force you to revere His transcendence instead of reducing Him to a location? Will you from now on be more mindful of how you speak about Allah's presence?
?
The Mu'tazila were intelligent, yet their reasoning led to blasphemy. Is there a belief about Allah that you hold based on your own logic rather than the Quran and Sunnah? What step will you take today to align your understanding with revelation?
?
If you truly believe Allah is exalted above all imperfections, how does that affect your worship? Does your daily life reflect awe and reverence for His transcendence, or do you treat Him as if He is near in a familiar, manageable way? What will you change starting today?

The Logical Contradiction of Being Everywhere
Al-Ash'ari uses a reductio to show the contradictory nature of the claim that Allah is everywhere.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses logical reasoning to show the impossibility of the claim that Allah is everywhere.

Core Idea
If Allah is everywhere, He would be both above and below, an impossibility.

Al-Ash'ari now presents a more formal logical argument. He assumes the opponents' position and shows that it leads to a self-contradictory situation where Allah would have to be both above and below simultaneously. This lesson analyzes that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the condition
Read the Arabic beginning with 'ويقال لهم' and notice the conditional structure: 'إذا لم يكن مستوياً على العرش... وكان الله في كل مكان'.
This sets up the opponents' view.
2
Follow the implications
Al-Ash'ari deduces that if Allah is everywhere, He is under the earth. Trace the logic: sky above earth, earth above ground, etc.
This is a spatial argument.
3
Identify the contradiction
The phrase 'فهو تحت ما هو فوقه وفوق ما هو تحته' captures the contradiction: He is under what is above Him and above what is under Him.
This is impossible for a single being.
4
Conclusion
Note the final exclamation: 'تعالى الله عن افترائكم' – Allah is exalted above your false attribution.
He ends with a declaration of transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعمت المعتزلة والحرورية والجهمية أن الله عز وجل في كل مكان فلزمهم أنه في بطن مريم وفي الحشوش والأخلية، وهذا خلاف الدين، تعالى الله عن قولهم علواً كبيراً.
جواب :
ويقال لهم : إذا لم يكن مستوياً على العرش بمعنى يختص العرش دون غيره كما قال ذلك أهل العلم ونقلة الآثار وحملة الأخبار، وكان الله عز وجل في كل مكان، فهو تحت الأرض التي السماء فوقها، وإذا كان تحت الأرض والأرض فوقه، والسماء فوق الأرض، ففي هذا ما يلزمكم أن تقولوا : إن الله تحت التحت والأشياء فوقه، وأنه فوق الفوق والأشياء تحته، وفي هذا ما يجب أنه تحت ما هو فوقه وفوق ما هو تحته، وهذا هو المحال المتناقض، تعالى الله عن افترائكم عليه علواً كبيراً.
The Mu'tazila, Haruriyya, and Jahmiyya claimed that Allah Almighty is in every place, so it necessarily follows that He is in the womb of Mary and in latrines and cesspits, and this is contrary to the religion. Exalted is Allah above their saying, greatly exalted.
Answer:

If He is under the earth and the earth is above Him, and the sky is above the earth, then this necessitates that you say: Allah is under the underneath and things are above Him, and that He is above the above and things are underneath Him, and this necessitates that He is under what is above Him and above what is underneath Him. This is impossible contradiction. Exalted is Allah above your falsehood against Him, greatly exalted.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Allah is everywhere. Al-Ash'ari first states the position of the Mu'tazila, Haruriyya (Kharijites), and Jahmiyya, who assert that Allah is in every place. He argues that this logically implies Allah would be in impure places like the womb of Mary and latrines, which is contrary to religious decency. Then he presents a reductio ad absurdum: if Allah is not specifically established on the Throne (istiwa') as the orthodox scholars hold, and He is everywhere, then He would be under the earth (since the sky is above the earth), leading to the contradictory situation of being both above and below simultaneously. Misconception: Some might think that if Allah is everywhere, He can be in multiple places at once without contradiction.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that literal spatial omnipresence leads to logical contradictions in a physical world with spatial relations.

Checkpoint

B) That Allah would be under the earth and above the sky simultaneously
C) That Allah would be in the heavens only
D) That Allah would be nowhere

Key Takeaway
Literal spatial omnipresence leads to logical impossibility, so the correct belief is that Allah is above His Throne in a way befitting His majesty.
