Refutation of the Jahmiyyah's Denial of Allah's Attributes
Imam Ash'ari refutes the Jahmiyyah for denying Allah's attributes and equating them with Christians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari refutes the Jahmiyyah for denying Allah's attributes and their agreement with the Christians in reducing attributes to mere knowledge.

Core Idea
Denying Allah's real attributes reduces Him to a mere knower, a view shared with the Christians.

Imam Ash'ari exposes the error of the Jahmiyyah who deny that Allah has a face, hearing, sight, and eyes. He points out that in doing so, they align with the Christians, who similarly reduce Allah's attributes of hearing and seeing to mere knowledge. This lesson shows the dangerous consequence of denying Allah's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the direct style of refutation.
The passage is a single argument comparing two sects.
2
Identify the denied attributes
Make a mental list of the attributes the Jahmiyyah deny: face, hearing, sight, eye. This is the core of their error.
They do not deny all attributes, only the ones that imply distinct realities.
3
Understand the comparison with Christians
Notice that the Jahmiyyah agree with the Christians in reducing 'hearing' and 'seeing' to mere knowledge. The passage explicitly states this parallel.
Imam Ash'ari highlights this to show that both groups strip Allah of His true attributes.
4
Reflect on the reductionist position
Consider why reducing attributes to knowledge is problematic. It denies the distinct realities that Allah has revealed about Himself.
The passage does not elaborate further, but it sets the stage for deeper theological debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: ونفت الجهمية أن يكون الله وجه كما قال وأبطلوا أن يكون له سمع وبصر وعين، ووافقوا النصارى؛ لأن النصارى لم تثبت الله سميعاً بصيراً إلا على معنى أنه عالم، وكذلك قالت الجهمية، ففي حقيقة قولهم أنهم قالوا: نقول إن الله عالم، ولا نقول سميع بصير على غير معنى عالم، وكذلك قول النصارى
Section: The Jahmiyyah denied that Allah has a face as He said, and they invalidated that He has hearing, sight, and an eye, and they agreed with the Christians; because the Christians did not affirm Allah as Hearing, Seeing except on the meaning that He is Knowing, and likewise the Jahmiyyah said. So in the reality of their statement: they said: 'We say that Allah is Knowing, but we do not say Hearing, Seeing with a meaning other than Knowing.' And likewise is the statement of the Christians.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This is a refutation section (fard) where Imam Ash'ari exposes the error of the Jahmiyyah. He states that the Jahmiyyah deny that Allah has a face, and they reject that He has hearing, sight, and eyes. Then he points out their agreement with the Christians, because the Christians do not affirm Allah as Hearing and Seeing except in the sense that He is Knowing (i.e., they reduce the attributes to knowledge). The Jahmiyyah say the same: they only affirm that Allah is 'Alim (Knowing) but refuse to affirm that He is Sami' (Hearing) and Basir (Seeing) as distinct attributes. The author concludes that the Jahmiyyah and Christians share this corrupted view, which strips Allah of the full reality of His attributes.

Key Terms
الجهمية
النصارى
عالم
سميع بصير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Jahmiyyah only deny the literal meaning of attributes but still affirm them in a sense.
Correction: The passage shows they deny the attributes as real distinct attributes, reducing them to mere knowledge, which is a denial of their reality.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, in what way did the Jahmiyyah agree with the Christians?
A) They both affirmed that Allah has a face
B) They both denied that Allah has attributes altogether
C) They both reduced the attributes of hearing and seeing to mere knowledge
D) They both claimed that Allah is in heaven

Key Takeaway
The Jahmiyyah deny Allah's attributes of face, hearing, sight, and eye, and in doing so they agree with the Christians in reducing His attributes to mere knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself thinking that Allah 'hears' your dua only in the sense that He knows what you said, rather than truly hearing it with a hearing that befits His majesty? If so, how can you train your heart to affirm the full reality of His attributes?
?
The Jahmiyyah and Christians both avoided affirming the literal attributes out of fear of anthropomorphism. Is there an attribute of Allah—like His hand, face, or descending—that you secretly feel uncomfortable affirming? What would it cost you to accept it as He described?
?
If you were to strip Allah of even one of His attributes in your heart, would you not be walking the same path as the Jahmiyyah? Today, resolve to repent from any subtle denial and say: 'I believe Allah is Hearing, Seeing, with a hearing and sight that are real and befitting His greatness.'

Refuting Jahmiyyah on Denial of Attributes
Al-Ash'ari refutes Jahmiyyah for denying face, hearing, sight, comparing them to Christians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari refutes the Jahmiyyah's denial of Allah's attributes by exposing their agreement with Christian theology.

Core Idea
Denying Allah's attributes echoes Christian error.

Al-Ash'ari confronts a deviant group, the Jahmiyyah, who reject Allah's literal attributes like Face, Hearing, and Sight. He reveals that their position is not new—it mirrors the Christians' flawed interpretation of these attributes as mere knowledge. This passage shows the danger of stripping Allah of His revealed names.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the key terms and the structure: first the denial, then the comparison to Christians.
The passage is a single paragraph containing a full argument.
2
Identify the groups
Note that al-Ash'ari directly links the Jahmiyyah to the Christians. Why is this comparison significant? It shows the Jahmiyyah are following an already refuted path.
3
Understand the refutation
The refutation works by exposing that the Jahmiyyah reduce distinct attributes to mere knowledge, just as Christians do. This contradicts the Quranic text that affirms separate attributes.
Ask yourself: What is the logical flaw in reducing 'Hearing' and 'Seeing' to only 'Knowing'?

The author exposes the reality of their position: they verbally say "Allah is Knowing" but refuse to say "Allah is Hearing, Seeing" in a sense other than "Knowing." This reduces the attributes to mere knowledge. The refutation is that the Quran affirms distinct attributes, and the Jahmiyyah are following the Christians' error.

Al-Ash'ari's Refutation of the Jahmiyyah on Divine Attributes
Al-Ash'ari accuses Jahmiyyah of denying all divine attributes, only concealing due to fear.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's accusation that the Jahmiyyah's denial of Allah's attributes amounts to nullification of tawhid and concealed heresy.

Core Idea
Denying Allah's attributes is not a minor opinion but a nullification of tawhid.

Al-Ash'ari directly confronts the Jahmiyyah sect, who claimed that Allah has no knowledge, power, hearing, or sight. In this passage, he exposes their true intentions and the fear that prevents them from openly declaring their rejection of Allah's names. This lesson examines the accusation and its theological weight.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the forceful tone and the author's direct accusation.
2
Identify the denied attributes
The Jahmiyyah deny knowledge, power, hearing, and sight. List them and consider why these are fundamental attributes in Islamic theology.
3
Understand 'تعطيل التوحيد'
Al-Ash'ari says their goal is to nullify tawhid. Reflect on how denying attributes undermines the very concept of tawhid.
4

The 'sword' likely refers to execution for apostasy.

The author then reveals that if not for fear of execution ('the sword'), they would openly declare that Allah is not Hearing, Seeing, or Knowing. Thus their heresy (zandaqa) is concealed. This is a harsh refutation, accusing them of hypocrisy and disbelief.

Refuting the Jahmi Claim of Identity Between Allah and His Knowledge
Al-Ash'ari refutes a Jahmi claim by showing its absurd consequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how equating Allah's knowledge with His essence leads to absurd consequences and actually denies the attribute.

Core Idea
Calling knowledge 'Allah' makes 'O Knowledge, forgive me!' an absurd prayer.

Al-Ash'ari presents a specific Jahmi claim: that Allah's knowledge is not a distinct attribute but identical to Allah Himself. He then reveals the logical absurdity of this claim, showing that it would force one to pray to 'Knowledge' for forgiveness. This refutation exposes the error of denying real attributes while pretending to affirm them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the structure: claim, analysis, absurd consequence, glorification.
The Arabic is concise; the translation expands slightly for clarity.
2
Identify the Jahmi leader's claim
What exactly did he claim? He said 'Allah's knowledge is Allah' and 'Allah is knowledge.'
3
Understand al-Ash'ari's analysis
Al-Ash'ari points out that this claim 'denies knowledge in a way that makes one think he affirmed it.' Why? Because if knowledge is identical to Allah, it is not a real attribute distinct from Him.
This is a key logical point.
4
See the absurd consequence
If knowledge is Allah, then calling upon 'Knowledge' for forgiveness would be like calling upon Allah. That is absurd because we are commanded to call upon Allah by His name, not by an attribute as if it were a separate entity.
Al-Ash'ari uses the example 'O Knowledge, forgive me!' to highlight the absurdity.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Al-Ash'ari ends by glorifying Allah above such statements. This shows that the proper response to such errors is not just rebuttal but also affirming Allah's transcendence.
This is a common pattern in kalam texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل :
وزعم شيخ منهم مقدم فيهم أن علم الله هو الله، وأن الله عز وجل علم، فنفى العلم من حيث أوهم أنه أثبته حتى ألزم أن يقول: يا علم اغفر لي ; إذ كان علم الله عنده هو الله، وكان الله - على قياسه - علماً وقدرة تعالى الله عما يقولون علواً كبيراً .
Section: And a leader among them, advanced among them, claimed that Allah's knowledge is Allah, and that Allah, Mighty and Majestic, is knowledge. So he denied knowledge in a way that made one think he affirmed it, until he was forced to say: 'O Knowledge, forgive me!' since Allah's knowledge according to him is Allah, and Allah—by his analogy—would be knowledge and power. Exalted is Allah above what they say, with great exaltation.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an extreme Jahmi position. Al-Ash'ari reports that a leader of the Jahmiyyah claimed that Allah's knowledge is identical to Allah (i.e., it is not an attribute distinct from the essence), and that Allah Himself is knowledge. The author points out that this effectively denies knowledge (as a real attribute), even though it appears to affirm it through identification. The absurd consequence is that if one were to ask forgiveness, one would have to say 'O Knowledge, forgive me!' because according to this view, knowledge is the same as Allah. Al-Ash'ari ends with glorifying Allah above such statements.

Key Terms
علم الله هو الله
قياس
شناعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think equating an attribute with the essence is a way to affirm it, but it actually denies the attribute.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that identity leads to absurdity; true affirmation requires distinction of attributes while acknowledging they are not separate from Allah.

Checkpoint
What absurd consequence does al-Ash'ari draw from the Jahmi leader's claim that Allah's knowledge is Allah?
A) One would have to pray to Allah alone
B) One would have to say 'O Knowledge, forgive me!'
C) One could not know Allah at all
D) One would become a polytheist

Key Takeaway
Equating an attribute with the essence destroys the distinction needed to affirm the attribute, leading to absurdities like praying to 'Knowledge'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refutation of the Jahmiyya on God's Attributes
Al-Ash'ari exposes the Jahmiyya's hypocrisy in denying God's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Jahmiyya sect hid their denial of God's attributes behind verbal affirmation and why Al-Ash'ari called them heretics.

Core Idea
The Jahmiyya verbally affirm God's attributes but truly deny their meaning.

Al-Ash'ari here exposes a dangerous deception. The Jahmiyya outwardly affirm that God has attributes like knowledge and power, but their actual belief is the opposite. He argues that their true intention is to nullify tawhid and deny God's names, and only fear of punishment prevents them from openly declaring their heresy. This passage teaches us to beware of those who say one thing but mean another.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once carefully. Notice the structure: first the claim of the Jahmiyya, then Al-Ash'ari's analysis of their true intention.
The key phrase is 'فأعطوا ذلك لفظاً، ولم يحصلوا قولاً في المعنى' – they gave words but not meaning.
2
Identify the four denied attributes
The Jahmiyya explicitly deny that God has knowledge, power, hearing, and sight. Note that these are four of the most fundamental attributes of God.
3
Understand their hidden intention
Al-Ash'ari states that their goal is to nullify tawhid and deny God's names. The verbal affirmation is a cover; their real position is denial.
They are performing a kind of taqiyya (dissimulation) out of fear.
4
Consider the role of fear
They would openly deny God's attributes if not for fear of the sword. This shows that their outward acceptance is not genuine.
The term 'zandaqa' (heresy) is used to describe their true belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So they gave that verbally, but did not achieve a statement in meaning. And were it not that they feared the sword, they would have declared plainly that God is not hearing, not seeing, not knowing. But fear of the sword prevented them from manifesting their heresy.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Jahmiyya sect. Al-Ash'ari exposes their hypocrisy: they verbally affirm God's attributes (knowledge, power, hearing, sight) but in meaning they negate them. Their goal is to invalidate tawhid and deny God's names. They speak words of affirmation, but their intended meaning is denial. If not for fear of physical punishment (the sword), they would openly state that God is not hearing, seeing, or knowing. Thus, their apparent affirmation is a ruse; the truth is their outright denial of attributes. The phrase 'zandaqa' (زندقة) accuses them of heresy.

Refuting the Identification of God's Knowledge with God
Al-Ash'ari refutes the claim that God's knowledge is God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why identifying God's attribute of knowledge with God Himself leads to absurd consequences.

Core Idea
To say God's knowledge is God reduces God to an attribute and leads to blasphemy.

In this passage, Al-Ash'ari exposes the logical outcome of a Jahmi claim that equates God's knowledge with God. By taking the claim to its conclusion, he shows that it would require invoking 'knowledge' as if it were a separate deity, thereby negating the attribute itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Al-Ash'ari presents the claim and then its consequence.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the claim and its implication
The Jahmi leader claims that God's knowledge is God. Al-Ash'ari points out that this effectively negates knowledge as a distinct attribute. What forced statement does he say follows from this claim?
Look for the phrase 'يا علم اغفر لي'.
3
Reflect on the refutation
Al-Ash'ari concludes by exclaiming God's transcendence. Why is this conclusion appropriate? How does the absurd consequence refute the original claim?
Consider how reductio ad absurdum works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : وزعم شيخ منهم مقدم فيهم أن علم الله هو الله، وأن الله عز وجل علم، فنفى العلم من حيث أوهم أنه أثبته حتى ألزم أن يقول: يا علم اغفر لي ؛ إذ كان علم الله عنده هو الله، وكان الله - على قياسه - علماً وقـدرة تعالى الله عما يقولون علواً كبيراً .

Commentary
This passage refutes a specific Jahmi claim: that God's knowledge is identical to God Himself. This claim effectively negates knowledge as an attribute, because by identifying it with God, they inadvertently imply that God is mere knowledge. Al-Ash'ari then adds that on their reasoning God would be 'knowledge and power' (i.e., reduced to attributes), and he exclaims God's transcendence above such statements.

The Jahmiyyah's Indirect Denial of Allah's Attributes
Al-Ash'ari exposes the Jahmiyyah's indirect denial of Allah's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Jahmiyyah denied Allah's attributes through indirect implication rather than open statement, and why they employed this deceptive method.

Core Idea
The Jahmiyyah denied Allah's attributes by implication, not openly.

In this passage, al-Ash'ari exposes the deceitful tactic of the Jahmiyyah sect. They claimed Allah has no knowledge, power, life, hearing, or sight. Their real aim was to deny that Allah is knowing, powerful, living, hearing, and seeing—i.e., to strip Him of His attributes. But they feared the sword (persecution or execution) if they openly stated this denial. So they used indirect expressions that necessarily imply the denial. Al-Ash'ari traces this trick to the Zanadiqa (heretics) and Mu'attila, who openly denied Allah's attributes. This lesson reveals the Jahmiyyah's method and its origins.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a claim, an intention, an obstacle, a method, an implication, and a source.
The Arabic ends with a corrupt phrase, but the main argument is clear.
2
Identify the Jahmiyyah's claim and real intention
The Jahmiyyah openly said Allah has no knowledge, power, etc. But what did they really want to deny? They wanted to deny that Allah is knowing, powerful, etc.—i.e., deny the very attributes. How do we know? Al-Ash'ari says 'they intended to deny that Allah is knowing, powerful...'
3
Understand why they used indirect language
Why didn't they just say 'Allah is not knowing'? Because fear of the sword prevented open denial. So they expressed the meaning indirectly: saying 'He has no knowledge' implies 'He is not knowing.' This is their deceptive method.
Al-Ash'ari highlights the logical entailment: if no knowledge, then not knowing.
4
Trace the source of this method
Al-Ash'ari says they took this from the people of zandaqa and ta'til. Recall that zanadiqa are heretics who openly denied Allah's attributes. This shows the Jahmiyyah are not original; they follow earlier heretical groups.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل : وزعمت الجهمية أن الله عز وجل لا علم له ولا قدرة ولا حياة ولا سمع ولا بصر، وأرادوا أن ينفوا أن الله تعالى عالم قادر حي سميع بصير، فمنعهم خوف السيف من إظهارهم نفي ذلك، فأتوا بمعناه ؛ لأنهم إذا قالوا لا علم الله ولا قدرة له، فقد قالوا: إنه ليس بعالم ولا قادر، وجب ذلك عليهم، وهذا إنما أخذوه عن أهل الزندقة والتعطيل ؛ لأن الزنادقة قد قال كثير منهم : إن الله تعالى ليس بعالم ولا قادر ولا حي ولا له [؟]
Section: And the Jahmiyyah claimed that Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, has no knowledge, no power, no life, no hearing, and no sight. And they intended to deny that Allah, the Most High, is knowing, powerful, living, hearing, and seeing. But the fear of the sword prevented them from openly denying that, so they expressed its meaning. Because when they say 'Allah has no knowledge and no power,' they have said: He is not knowing and not powerful, and that is necessarily entailed upon them. And they only took this from the people of zandaqa (heresy) and ta'til (denial of attributes), for many of the zanadiqa have said that Allah, the Most High, is not knowing, not powerful, not living, and not [possessing]...
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage explains the deceptive method of the Jahmiyyah. They claimed that Allah has no knowledge, power, life, hearing, or sight. Their real aim was to deny that Allah is knowing, powerful, living, hearing, and seeing—i.e., to deny His attributes and thus His actual names. However, they were afraid of the sword (i.e., persecution or execution by the authorities) if they openly stated this denial. So they instead used indirect expressions: saying 'Allah has no knowledge' implies 'He is not knowing.' Al-Ash'ari traces this trick to the Zanadiqa (heretics) and the Mu'attila (those who strip Allah of attributes), who openly denied that Allah is knowing, powerful, living, etc. The passage shows that the Jahmiyyah's method was to hide their true belief while still expressing it through implication.

Key Terms
الجهمية
الزندقة
التعطيل
علم
قدرة
حياة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Jahmiyyah only denied specific attributes like hand or face; this shows they denied even knowledge and power.
Correction: The passage explicitly states they denied knowledge, power, life, hearing, and sight, which are core attributes. Their denial was not limited to anthropomorphic attributes but struck at the very essence of Allah's perfection.

Checkpoint
Why did the Jahmiyyah deny Allah's attributes indirectly rather than openly?
A) They were unsure of their position
B) Fear of the sword prevented them
C) They wanted to avoid logical contradictions
D) They followed the Quran's ambiguous verses

Key Takeaway
The Jahmiyyah's denial of attributes was not a superficial error but a calculated deception rooted in heretical predecessors, using indirect language to avoid punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jahmiyyah feared the sword of human authorities. What do you fear that stops you from openly affirming Allah's attributes as He revealed them, even when they contradict popular or comfortable ideas? Will you repent of that fear and speak the truth, regardless of consequences?
?
When you read that the Jahmiyyah used indirect language to deny Allah's attributes, do you recognize any area of your life where you avoid saying what you truly believe about Allah because it might be unpopular or inconvenient? How will you change that starting today?
?
If you were put in a situation where affirming Allah's attributes could cost you your livelihood or reputation, would you still affirm them? What does your honest answer reveal about the strength of your iman, and what will you do to strengthen it?

The Jahmiyyah's Hidden Denial of Attributes
Imam Ash'ari exposes the Jahmiyyah's disguised denial of divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Jahmiyyah and Mu'tazilah denied the reality of divine attributes while verbally affirming the names, a tactic rooted in zandaqah.

Core Idea
Affirming names without realities is a disguised denial of Allah's attributes.

Imam Ash'ari exposes a deceptive tactic: some groups claim to affirm that Allah is Knowing, Powerful, etc., but they deny the actual realities of knowledge and power. This passage reveals the historical and theological root of this maneuver, tracing it to the Zanadiqah and showing why it is a form of ta'til (negation).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key groups mentioned: Jahmiyyah, Zanadiqah, Mu'tazilah.
2
Identify the three groups and their claims
The passage names three groups. For each, note what they affirm or deny about Allah's attributes.
The Jahmiyyah deny the attributes outright; the Zanadiqah deny the names; the Mu'tazilah affirm names but deny realities.
3
Understand the 'fear of the sword'
Why did these groups not openly deny attributes? The passage says 'fear of the sword' prevented them. Reflect on how this led to their ambiguous language.
This is a key insight into their strategy.
4
Grasp the concept of 'tasmiah' without 'haqiqah'
The Mu'tazilah affirmed the names (tasmiah) but not the realities (haqiqah). Why is this insufficient? Think about what it means to truly affirm an attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: وزعمت الجهمية أن الله عز وجل لا علم له ولا قدرة ولا حياة ولا سمع ولا بصر، وأرادوا أن ينفوا أن الله تعالى عالم قادر حي سميع بصير، فمنعهم خوف السيف من إظهارهم نفي ذلك، فأتوا بمعناه؛ لأنهم إذا قالوا لا علم الله ولا قدرة له، فقد قالوا: إنه ليس بعالم ولا قادر، وجب ذلك عليهم، وهذا إنما أخذوه عن أهل الزندقة والتعطيل؛ لأن الزنادقة قد قال كثير منهم: إن الله تعالى ليس بعالم ولا قادر ولا حي ولا بصير، فلم تقدر المعتزلة أن تفصح بذلك فأتت بمعناه، وقالت: إن الله عالم قادر حي سميع بصير من طريق التسمية من غير أن يثبتوا له حقيقة العلم والقدرة والسمع والبصر.
The Jahmiyyah claimed that Allah has no knowledge, no power, no life, no hearing, and no sight, and they intended to deny that Allah is knowing, powerful, living, hearing, and seeing, but the fear of the sword prevented them from openly manifesting that denial, so they expressed its meaning; because if they say 'Allah has no knowledge and no power,' they have said that He is not knowing and not powerful—that necessarily follows for them. And this they only took from the people of zandaqah and ta'til (negation of attributes); because many of the Zanadiqah said that Allah is not knowing, not powerful, not living, and not seeing. So the Mu'tazilah were not able to state that plainly, so they expressed its meaning, and said: 'Allah is knowing, powerful, living, hearing, seeing' by way of naming, without affirming for Him the reality of knowledge, power, hearing, and sight.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage exposes the deceptive tactic of the Jahmiyyah and the Mu'tazilah. They denied the reality of divine attributes while verbally affirming the names. The author explains that they feared persecution ('fear of the sword') so they could not openly deny attributes, instead they used ambiguous language. He traces this denial back to the Zanadiqah (heretics). The key point: their verbal affirmation of names like 'Knowing' and 'Powerful' is meaningless because they do not affirm the corresponding realities. This is a refutation of those who claim that mere verbal profession is sufficient.

Misconception: Simply saying 'Allah is Knowing' is sufficient, even if one denies the reality of His knowledge.
Correction: The passage shows that affirming the name without the attribute's reality is a form of denial inherited from the Zanadiqah.

Refuting the Identity of Attribute and Essence: The Case of Abu al-Hudhayl
Imam Ash'ari refutes Abu al-Hudhayl's claim by exposing its logical contradiction and establishing a general rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that Allah's knowledge is identical to His essence leads to absurdity and why the attribute and the one qualified must be distinct yet inseparable.

Core Idea
Affirming an attribute without its subject is as contradictory as affirming a subject without its attribute.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari's al-Ibanah tackles a specific Mu'tazili claim that collapses the distinction between Allah and His attribute of knowledge. By examining Abu al-Hudhayl's position and the logical response, we learn a fundamental principle of Sunni orthodoxy: attributes are not identical to the essence but are necessarily entailed by it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim
Read the passage to find what Abu al-Hudhayl claimed about Allah's knowledge. Note that he said 'Allah's knowledge is Allah,' making the attribute identical to the essence.
2
The Refutation Example
The author presents a concrete test: if knowledge is Allah, one could pray to 'knowledge' for forgiveness. Abu al-Hudhayl refused to do so, revealing the contradiction in his position.
This shows that the claim leads to absurd practical consequences.
3
Extract the General Principle
After the example, the author states a logical rule: you cannot affirm a knower without knowledge, nor knowledge without a knower. This applies to all attributes like power, life, etc.
The principle is about the mutual dependence of attribute and subject.
4
Apply the Principle to Other Attributes
The passage explicitly extends the rule to other attributes: power, life, hearing, sight. Consider why the same logic holds for each pair.
This reinforces the general nature of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: وقد قال رئيس من رؤسائهم — وهو أبو الهذيل العلاف — إن علم الله هو الله، فجعل الله تعالى علماً. وأُلْزِمَ، فقيل له: إذا قلت إن علم الله هو الله فقل: يا علم الله اغفر لي وارحمني، فأبى ذلك، فلزمه المناقضة. واعلموا — رحمكم الله — أن من قال عالم ولا علم كان مناقضاً، كما أن من قال علم ولا عالم كان مناقضاً، وكذلك القول في القدرة والقادر، والحياة والحي، والسمع والبصر والسميع والبصير.
A chief of their leaders — Abu al-Hudhayl al-Allaf — said that Allah's knowledge is Allah, thus he made Allah knowledge. And he was compelled, and it was said to him: 'If you say that Allah's knowledge is Allah, then say: O knowledge of Allah, forgive me and have mercy on me.' But he refused that, so contradiction followed him. And know — may Allah have mercy on you — that whoever says 'knowing without knowledge' is contradictory, just as whoever says 'knowledge without knowing' is contradictory, and similarly for power and powerful, life and living, hearing and seeing, and the hearer and the seer.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage presents a specific historical example and a general logical principle. Abu al-Hudhayl al-Allaf, a Mu'tazili leader, claimed that Allah's knowledge is identical to Allah's essence. The author shows the absurdity: if knowledge is Allah, one could pray to 'knowledge' for forgiveness, but Abu al-Hudhayl refused to do so, revealing the contradiction. The general rule follows: the attribute (e.g., knowledge) and the one qualified by it (e.g., knowing) are distinct but necessarily co-implicate. You cannot affirm the derived name without affirming the attribute, nor vice versa. This applies to all attributes like power, life, hearing, and sight.

Key Terms
أبو الهذيل العلاف
العلم
المناقضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that attributes like knowledge are identical to the divine essence, so there is no distinction.
Correction: The passage shows that if knowledge were identical to the essence, then praying to 'knowledge' would be praying to Allah, but Abu al-Hudhayl's refusal shows the contradiction. Attributes are distinct from the essence yet inseparable.

Checkpoint
What was the example used to show the contradiction in Abu al-Hudhayl's claim?
A) Calling on knowledge to forgive
B) Denying power
C) Affecting life
D) Saying God is not powerful

Key Takeaway
An attribute and its subject are distinct but necessarily coexist; denying either is a contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you were to explain the relationship between Allah and His attributes to a doubter, would you be able to defend the middle path as shown by Imam Ash'ari? What step of the proof do you need to internalize first?

The Analogical Proof for Real Attributes
Imam Ash'ari uses analogy from speech to argue that attributes must be real.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari uses analogy and consensus to prove that Allah's attributes are real entities, not mere names.

Core Idea
Denying real attributes contradicts both reason and early Muslim consensus.

Imam Ash'ari presents a powerful argument: if claiming Allah speaks without speech is contradictory, then claiming He knows without knowledge is equally contradictory. He then strengthens this by citing the consensus of early Muslims before the rise of theological sects. This passage uses both logical analogy and historical authority to defend the reality of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the rhetorical question and the forceful conclusion.
The passage is a direct rebuttal to those who deny attributes.
2
Identify the analogy
Find the comparison between speech and knowledge. How does the author use the opponent's own admission against them?
The analogy is: if speaking implies speech, then knowing implies knowledge.
3
Note the consensus argument
Observe that the author cites the consensus of early Muslims before the emergence of heretical sects. Why is this important?
Consensus (ijma') is a strong proof in Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب: ويقال لهم: خبرونا عمن زعم أن الله متكلم قائل آمر ناه، لا قول له ولا كلام ولا أمر له ولا نهي، أليس هو مناقض خارج عن جملة المسلمين؟ فلا بد من نعم، فيقال لهم: فكذلك من قال: إن الله تعالى عالم ولا علم له كان ذلك مناقضاً خارجاً عن جملة المسلمين. وقد أجمع المسلمون قبل حدوث الجهمية والمعتزلة والحرورية على أن لله علماً لم يزل، وقد قالوا: علم الله لم يزل، وعلم الله سابق في الأشياء.
Answer: And it is said to them: Inform us about one who claims that Allah is speaking, saying, commanding, forbidding, but He has no speech, no words, no command, and no prohibition — is he not contradictory, outside the fold of the Muslims? There is no alternative but to say 'yes.' So it is said to them: Likewise, whoever says that Allah is knowing but He has no knowledge, that is contradictory, outside the fold of the Muslims. And the Muslims were unanimous before the emergence of the Jahmiyyah, Mu'tazilah, and Haruriyyah that Allah has eternal knowledge, and they said: Allah's knowledge is eternal, and Allah's knowledge precedes things.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument (jadal) using analogy. The author challenges the opponent: if someone claims Allah speaks without speech, that is clearly contradictory. The opponent must agree. Then the author applies the same logic: claiming Allah is knowing without knowledge is equally contradictory. He then cites the consensus (ijma') of the early Muslims before the emergence of the Jahmiyyah, Mu'tazilah, and Haruriyyah that Allah has eternal knowledge. This shows that the denial of attributes is an innovation contrary to the established Sunni position.

Key Terms
الجهمية
المعتزلة
الحرورية
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think affirming attributes is a later innovation or that attributes are mere names.
Correction: The passage shows that early Muslims unanimously affirmed that Allah has real, eternal knowledge, and that the heretical sects arose later.

Checkpoint
What group is not mentioned as emerging after the early consensus?
A) Jahmiyyah
B) Mu'tazilah
C) Haruriyyah
D) Ash'ariyyah

Key Takeaway
The reality of Allah's attributes is proven both by logical consistency and by the consensus of early Muslims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about Allah that conveniently avoided fully attributing real, eternal knowledge and speech to Him, perhaps thinking it too anthropomorphic? How does this lesson expose that as a logical and communal contradiction? What will you change in your inner conviction today?
?
Imam Ash'ari uses the early Muslim consensus to prove that affirming attributes is not an innovation. Do you truly anchor your beliefs on the consensus of the salaf, or do you sometimes prefer modern reinterpretations that feel more comfortable? Will you commit to checking your beliefs against the early consensus from now on?
?
If denying Allah's real knowledge is as contradictory as denying His speech, then every moment you treat His knowledge as abstract or metaphorical, you are veering toward that contradiction. What specific thought or action today will you use to remind yourself that Allah's knowledge is real, eternal, and fully present?

The Mu'tazila Interpretation of Sami' and Basir
Al-Ash'ari reports the Mu'tazila interpretation of 'Sami' and 'Basir' as meaning 'Alim'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila claim that God's names 'Sami'' and 'Basir' simply mean 'Alim', and the theological significance of this reduction.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila reduce God's hearing and sight to His knowledge.

In this passage, Al-Ash'ari reports the view of the Mu'tazila regarding two of God's beautiful names. They interpret 'Sami'' (All-Hearing) and 'Basir' (All-Seeing) as merely meaning 'Alim' (All-Knowing). This is a key point of contention because it denies that God has distinct attributes of hearing and sight separate from His knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic sentence and its translation. Note that this is a report of the opponent's position, not Al-Ash'ari's own view.
2
Understand the claim

3
Consider the significance

And the Mu'tazila claimed that the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Sami'un (Hearing) Basirun (Seeing)' [Quran 22:11] — its meaning is 'Alimun (Knowing).'

This short passage reports a doctrinal position of the Mu'tazila. They interpret the divine names 'Sami' (Hearing) and 'Basir' (Seeing) as merely meaning 'Alim' (Knowing), thereby denying that God has distinct attributes of hearing and sight separate from knowledge. This is a key point of contention between the Ash'aris and Mu'tazila. The Irony of the Name 'Qadariyya'
Imam Ash'ari rebuts Mu'tazila's claim about the name Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the irony in the Mu'tazila's claim that Ash'arites deserve the name Qadariyya, and the historical usage of the term.

Core Idea
The term 'Qadariyya' was for those who deny divine decree, not those who affirm it.

This passage exposes a terminological inconsistency. The Mu'tazila, who are called Qadariyya by others, themselves claim that the Ash'arites deserve that name because they affirm that Allah decrees evil. But the author points out that the name's origin is actually tied to denying predestination, making the Mu'tazila the true Qadariyya.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the direct claim by the Qadariyya (Mu'tazila).
The passage is short but dense with sectarian implications.
2
Identify the claim and the irony
The Mu'tazila say 'we deserve the name Qadari because we say Allah decrees evil and disbelief.' But historically, the label was used for those who reject divine decree. Reflect on the contradiction.
3
Connect to the broader debate
Ask yourself: Why would the Mu'tazila want to claim that name? What does this reveal about their strategy? The commentary will help clarify.
This connects to the learning objective about terminological accuracy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۲۴ - مسألة : وزعمت القدرية أنا نستحق اسم القدر ؛ لأنا نقول: إن الله عز وجل قدر الشر والكفر، فمن يثبت القدر كان قدرياً دون من لم يثبته .
224 - Issue: And the Qadariyya claimed that we deserve the name 'Qadar' (predestination) because we say: Indeed Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has decreed evil and disbelief. So whoever affirms predestination (al-qadr) is a Qadari, not the one who does not affirm it.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a brief but pointed clarification regarding the name 'Qadariyya.' The Mu'tazila, who are known as Qadariyya (literally 'those who affirm divine decree'), ironically claim that the Ash'arites deserve this label because the Ash'arites affirm that Allah decrees evil and disbelief. The author exposes the Mu'tazila's inconsistency: the term 'Qadari' was historically applied to those who deny predestination (as in the hadith 'the Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation'), not to those who affirm it. The Mu'tazila want to reverse the naming, but the author points out that if the name is derived from affirming al-qadr (divine decree), then the Ash'arites, who affirm it, are more deserving. However, the actual usage in Islamic tradition is that 'Qadariyya' refers to those who reject predestination, so the Mu'tazila's claim is self-serving. This passage serves as a terminological rebuttal.

Key Terms
القدرية
القدر
الشر
الكفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The name 'Qadariyya' means those who affirm divine predestination.
Correction: In early Islam, the term 'Qadariyya' was applied to those who denied divine decree, not those who affirmed it.

Checkpoint

A) That it applies to those who deny predestination.
B) That it applies to those who affirm that God decrees evil.
C) That the Ash'arites are the true Qadariyya.
D) That the name has no basis.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's attempt to rename the Ash'arites as Qadariyya fails because historically the term belongs to those who deny divine decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Mu'tazila tried to redefine 'Qadariyya' to suit their agenda. When have you twisted the meaning of a religious term to avoid a hard truth about your own faith? What would it cost you to accept the term as it was originally intended?

Refuting the Mu'tazila by Comparison to Magians
Al-Ash'ari refutes Mu'tazila by comparing them to Magians and citing a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari refutes the Mu'tazila by showing their doctrine parallels and exceeds the Magian belief in attributing power to other than Allah.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila are worse than the Magians: both give others power Allah lacks.

Al-Ash'ari employs a powerful rhetorical argument by comparing the Mu'tazila to the Magians. The Magians claimed Satan can do evil that Allah cannot; the Mu'tazila claim disbelievers can do disbelief that Allah cannot. This passage reveals that the Mu'tazila not only share the Magian error but exceed it, and a prophetic hadith confirms the parallel.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the rhetorical question and the structure: first the Magian claim, then the Mu'tazila claim, then the hadith.
Pay attention to the word 'زدتم' (you have exceeded) – this is the key point.
2
Identify the two claims
Find the Magian claim about Satan and the Mu'tazila claim about disbelievers. How are they similar? How does the Mu'tazila claim 'exceed' the Magian claim?
The Magians limit Allah's power over evil; the Mu'tazila limit His power over disbelief, and they apply it to all disbelievers, not just a single being.
3
Understand the hadith proof
Read the hadith: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah.' Why does this prove the comparison? Because the Qadariyya (deniers of predestination) share the Magian belief in a power independent of Allah.
Al-Ash'ari uses the hadith to show that this is not merely a logical argument but rooted in revelation.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Ask yourself: What does this argument teach about divine omnipotence? How does it guard against compromising Allah's power?
This lesson reinforces the Sunni position that Allah is the sole creator and controller of all actions, good and evil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرد على المعتزلة : قال الشيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري رحمة الله عليه: ويقال لهم : أليس المجوس أثبتوا أن الشيطان يقدر على الشر الذي لا يقدر الله عز وجل عليه فكانوا بقولهم هذا كافرين ؟ فلا بد من نعم . فيقال لهم : فإذا زعمتم أن الكافرين يقدرون على الكفر، والله عز وجل لا يقدر عليه، فقد زدتم على المجوس في قولكم ؛ لأنكم تقولون معهم : إن الشيطان يقدر على الشر والله لا يقدر عليه وهذا مما يبينه الخبر عن رسول الله : (إِنَّ القَدَرِيَةَ مَجُوسُ هَذه الأمة ) ، وإنما صاروا مجوس هذه الأمة لأنهم قالوا بقول المجوس .
Refutation of the Mu'tazila: Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, may Allah have mercy on him, said: And it is said to them: Did not the Magians affirm that Satan is able to do evil which Allah Almighty is not able to do, and thus they became disbelievers by this statement of theirs? So they must say 'yes'. Then it is said to them: So when you claim that the disbelievers are able to disbelief, and Allah Almighty is not able to it, then you have exceeded the Magians in your statement, because you say along with them: that Satan is able to evil and Allah is not able to it. And this is clarified by the report from the Messenger of Allah: 'Indeed the Qadariyya are the Magians of this Ummah', and they only became the Magians of this Ummah because they said the statement of the Magians.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila by exposing a parallel between their doctrine and that of the Magians. The Magians claimed that Satan can do evil that God cannot. Similarly, the Mu'tazila claim that disbelievers can perform disbelief that God cannot. The Ash'ari points out that if the Magians are disbelievers for this, then the Mu'tazila are even worse because they add the assignment of power to humans alongside Satan. The proof from the hadith identifies the Qadariyya (those who deny predestination) as the Magians of this Ummah, confirming the comparison.

Key Terms
المجوس
الشيطان
القدرية
الكفر
الشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila are only slightly mistaken about free will, but not as bad as polytheists.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows they exceed the Magians in disbelief because they give humans a power that rivals Allah's, similar to how Magians give Satan power over evil.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Ash'ari say the Mu'tazila exceed the Magians?
A) Because the Mu'tazila deny God's power over good.
B) Because the Mu'tazila claim that disbelievers can do what God cannot, just as Magians claim about Satan, and they say it about humans as well.
C) Because the Mu'tazila affirm God's power over evil.
D) Because the Mu'tazila are not monotheists.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila exceed the Magians in disbelief by claiming that disbelievers can do what Allah cannot, thereby compromising Allah's absolute power.

?

?
Have you ever doubted Allah's absolute power over all events, including evil, by saying 'Why did Allah allow this?' in a way that implies He was unable to stop it? What must you change in your heart after learning this?
?
If you truly believe that no one can do anything without Allah's will, how would your trust in Him reshape the way you face your greatest weakness today?

Definition of Qadari and Refutation of Opponents
Defines the term Qadari and argues the opponents are the true Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the polemical definition of 'Qadari' as used by Imam al-Ash'ari and how he turns the label back on his opponents.

Core Idea
The true Qadari claims to determine his own actions without Allah.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari's al-Ibanah presents a key theological argument about who deserves the label 'Qadari.' Rather than accepting the opponents' self-identification, al-Ash'ari redefines the term based on linguistic analogy and applies it to those who deny divine determination of actions. The passage is a masterclass in turning the tables through precise definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Notice the structure: definition, linguistic analogy, application to opponents, and the author's own position.
2
Understand the definition
The author defines 'Qadari' as one who affirms predetermination (al-qadr) for himself, not for Allah.
This reverses the common usage of the term.
3
Analyze the linguistic analogy
The silversmith and carpenter examples show how language works: a craftsman is named by what he claims to do himself.
The analogy clarifies that the opponents are called Qadari because they claim to determine their own actions.
4
See the application
The opponents claim to determine their actions apart from Allah, so they are the Qadariyya. The author's group attributes all actions to Allah.
5
Reflect on the polemical move
This redefinition reverses the accusation, a common strategy in sectarian debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقال لهم : القدري هو من يثبت القدر لنفسه دون ربه عز وجل، وأنه يقدر أفعاله دون خالقه، وكذلك هو في اللغة؛ لأن الصائغ هو من زعم أنه يصوغ دون من يقول إنه يصاغ له، والنجار هو من يضيف النجارة إلى نفسه دون من يزعم أنه ينجر له، فلما كنتم تزعمون أنكم تقدرون أعمالكم وتفعلونها دون ربكم وجب أن تكونوا قدرية ولم نكن نحن قدرية ؛ لأنا لم نضف الأعمال إلى أنفسنا دون ربنا عز وجل، ولم نقل إنا نقدرها دونه، وقلنا: إنها تقدر لنا .
It is said to them: The Qadari is the one who affirms predetermination (al-qadr) for himself apart from his Lord, and that he determines his actions apart from his Creator. Similarly, it is in language: because the silversmith is the one who claims that he silvers without [attribution to] the one who says it is silvered for him, and the carpenter is the one who attributes carpentry to himself apart from the one who claims that it is carpentered for him. Since you claim that you determine (taqdirun) your actions and do them apart from your Lord, it is necessary that you be Qadariyya, and we are not Qadariyya, because we do not attribute actions to ourselves apart from our Lord, and we do not say that we determine them apart from Him; rather we say: they are determined (tuqaddaru) for us.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a definition and refutation. It begins by defining 'al-Qadari' as one who attributes predetermination (al-qadr) to himself rather than to Allah. The author then provides a linguistic analogy: just as a silversmith is called such because he claims to do the silversmithing without attributing it to another, so the opponent is called Qadari because he claims to determine his own actions without Allah. The author distinguishes his own position: they do not attribute actions to themselves but say actions are determined for them by Allah. Thus, the opponents are truly the Qadariyya, not the author's group.

Key Terms
قدري (Qadari)
القدر (al-qadr)
تقرير (taqdir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term Qadari refers to those who affirm divine predestination.
Correction: Imam al-Ash'ari defines Qadari as those who claim to determine their own actions without Allah, not those who affirm predestination.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Ashari, why are the opponents called 'Qadariyya'?
A) Because they affirm that Allah predestines all actions.
B) Because they claim to determine their own actions apart from Allah.
C) Because they deny predestination entirely.
D) Because they attribute carpentry to themselves.

Key Takeaway
The polemical label 'Qadari' is applied by Imam al-Ash'ari to those who claim to determine their own actions independently of Allah, using linguistic analogy to reverse the accusation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed in a good deed, do you first thank Allah or quietly credit your own effort? Where does your heart go in that moment?
?
If you were to honestly trace every decision you made today back to its true source, would you find more of your own will or Allah's determination? What does that reveal about your reliance on Him?
?
You have just learned that the true Qadari is one who attributes actions to himself apart from Allah. Do you ever, even subtly, live as if your life is in your own hands? Will you today repent of that independence and declare that every action is determined for you?

Refuting the Qadari Accusation
Replies to the counter-argument that affirming Allah's predestination makes one Qadari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses a reductio ad absurdum to refute the claim that affirming divine predestination makes one a Qadari.

Core Idea
If affirming Allah's predestination made one a Qadari, the accusers would be Qadari themselves.

In this brief but powerful rejoinder, Imam al-Ash'ari turns the opponents' logic against them. He shows that their own definition—if applied consistently—would force them to accept the very label they reject. This passage is a masterclass in theological argumentation, using the opponent's own premises to undermine their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully. Then read the literal translation to get the plain meaning. Pay attention to the logical structure: 'if...then...'.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent claims that affirming Allah's predestination (taqdir) makes one a Qadari. Note this as the premise being challenged.
This is the starting point of the rejoinder.
3
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Al-Ash'ari shows that the opponent's own belief includes affirming Allah's predestination of the heavens, earth, and acts of obedience. Therefore, by their own logic, they would be Qadariyya. Since they reject this label, their initial claim is invalid.
This is the core logical move.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that the opponent's argument is self-refuting. Affirming Allah's taqdir does not make one a Qadari; rather, it is a necessary belief. The earlier definition (that Qadari are those who claim predestination for themselves) stands.
The rejoinder is complete and forceful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب : ويقال لهم : إذا كان من أثبت التقدير الله عز وجل قدرياً، فيلزمكم إذا زعمتم أن الله عز وجل قدر السموات والأرض وقدر الطاعات أن تكونوا قدرية، فإذا لم يلزم هذا فقد بطل قولكم وانتقض كلامكم
Answer: And it is said to them: If the one who affirms predetermination (al-taqdir) to Allah is a Qadari, then it follows that when you claim that Allah predetermined the heavens and the earth and predetermined acts of obedience, you become Qadariyya. If this does not follow, then your statement is invalidated and your speech is contradicted.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an answer (jawab) to a potential objection. The author employs a reductio ad absurdum: if affirming predetermination (al-taqdir) to Allah made one a Qadari, then the opponents themselves would be Qadari because they affirm that Allah predetermined the heavens, earth, and acts of obedience. Since they do not accept this label, their own criterion is self-refuting. Thus, the earlier definition stands: the Qadari is not one who affirms Allah's predetermination, but one who claims it for himself.

Key Terms
تقدير (taqdir)
قدرية (Qadariyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that affirming Allah's predestination is the defining feature of the Qadari sect.
Correction: This rejoinder shows that if that were the case, the opponents themselves would be Qadari for affirming Allah's predestination. The correct definition is that the Qadari is one who claims predestination for himself (i.e., denies divine decree).

Checkpoint
In the rejoinder, what consequence does Imam Ashari draw if the opponents' definition of Qadari were correct?
A) The opponents would be Qadariyya for affirming Allah's predestination.
B) The author's group would be Qadariyya for affirming Allah's predestination.
C) The definition would be proven correct.
D) The linguistic analogy would be invalid.

Key Takeaway
The rejoinder refutes the accusation by showing that if affirming divine predestination made one a Qadari, the accusers would be Qadari themselves, thus their argument is self-contradictory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are falsely accused of a wrong belief, do you immediately become defensive, or do you pause to examine whether the accusation actually applies to the accuser? This lesson teaches a precise logical move. How will you train yourself to respond with clarity rather than emotion the next time you face such a situation?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah's predestination includes all things—even your acts of obedience? If so, have you ever felt that this belief might be used against you by someone who misunderstands? How does this passage equip you to answer such objections with confidence and precision?
?
The opponent's argument collapsed because they held a double standard. Is there an area of your life where you judge others by a standard you do not apply to yourself? Let this passage's logic expose any inconsistency in your own heart, and commit to removing it today.

Allah's Foreknowledge: The Hadith of Adam and Musa
Imam Ash'ari cites the hadith of Adam and Musa to refute the Qadariyya claim of limited divine knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of Adam and Musa refutes the Qadariyya claim that Allah only knows events after they occur.

Core Idea
Allah's writing of destiny before creation proves His eternal knowledge.

Imam Ash'ari begins his refutation by citing a famous hadith in which Adam argues with Musa that his sin was written by Allah before the heavens were created. This hadith directly challenges the Qadariyya who assert that Allah does not know something until it happens. The author then draws the logical conclusion: if Allah wrote it, He must have known it.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the author's comment
Read the Arabic passage containing the hadith of Adam and Musa and the author's statement that it indicates the falsehood of the Qadariyya claim. Notice how the hadith is used as a proof.
2
Understand the Qadariyya claim
Identify the Qadariyya position: that Allah does not know the thing until it comes to be. Contrast this with the hadith's implication.
The Qadariyya were an early sect that denied predestination.
3
Analyze the logical inference
The author argues: if Allah wrote the deed and commanded it to be written, He cannot write something He does not know. Therefore, the hadith proves Allah's foreknowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الَّذِي اصْطَفَاكَ الله بِكَلَامِهِ، تَلُومُنِي عَلَى عَمَلٍ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ عَلَيَّ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ، قَالَ: فَحَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى. وَرُوِيَ حَدِيثُ حَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى مَالِكٌ عَنْ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَنِ الأَعْرَجِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ. وَهَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى بُطْلَانِ قَوْلِ الْقَدَرِيَّةِ الَّذِينَ يَقُولُونَ: إِنَّ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ لَا يَعْلَمُ الشَّيْءَ حَتَّى يَكُونَ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ إِذَا كَتَبَ ذَلِكَ وَأَمَرَ بِأَنْ يُكْتَبَ فَلَا يَكْتُبُ شَيْئًا لَا يَعْلَمُهُ، جَلَّ عَنْ ذَلِكَ وَتَقَدَّسَ. وَقَالَ اللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: ﴿وَمَا نَسْقُطُ مِن وَرَقَةٍ إِلَّا يَعْلَمُهَا وَلَا حَبَّةٍ فِي ظُلُمَتِ الْأَرْضِ وَلَا رَطْبٍ وَلَا يَابِسٍ إِلَّا فِي كِتَبٍ مُّبِينٍ﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿وَمَا مِن دَابَّةٍ فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا عَلَى اللهِ رِزْقُهَا وَيَعْلَمُ مُسْتَقَرَّهَا وَمُسْتَوْدَعَهَا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿أَحْصَاهُ اللهُ وَنَسُوهُ﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿لَقَدْ أَحْصَاهُمْ وَعَدَّهُمْ عَدًّا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿أَحَاطَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عِلْمًا وَأَحْصَى كُلَّ شَيْءٍ عَدَدًا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ﴾ فَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّهُ يَعْلَمُ الْأَشْيَاءَ كُلَّهَا. وَقَدْ أَخْبَرَ اللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ أَنَّ الْخَلْقَ يُبْعَثُونَ وَيُحْشَرُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْكَافِرِينَ فِي النَّارِ يُخَلَّدُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْأَنْبِيَاءَ وَالْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي الْجِنَانِ يُخَلَّدُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْقِيَامَةَ تَقُومُ وَلَمْ تَقُمِ الْقِيَامَةُ بَعْدُ، فَذَلِكَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى يَعْلَمُ مَا يَكُونَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَكُونَ. وَقَدْ قَالَ اللهُ فِي أَهْلِ النَّارِ: ﴿وَلَوْ رُدُّوا لَعَادُوا لِمَا نُهُوا عَنْهُ﴾ فَأَخْبَرَ عَمَّا لَا يَكُونُ أَنْ لَوْ كَانَ كَيْفَ يَكُونُ. وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَمَا بَالُ الْقُرُونِ الْأُولَى قَالَ عِلْمُهَا عِندَ رَبِّي فِي كِتَبٍ لَّا يَضِلُّ رَبِّي وَلَا يَنسَى﴾ وَمَنْ لَا يَعْلَمُ الشَّيْءَ قَبْلَ كَوْنِهِ لَا يَعْلَمُ بَعْدَ تَقَضِّيهِ، تَعَالَى اللهُ عَنْ قَوْلِ الظَّالِمِينَ عُلُوًّا كَبِيرًا.
He whom Allah chose with His speech, you blame me for a deed that Allah wrote upon me before He created the heavens. He said: So Adam argued with Musa. And the hadith of Adam arguing with Musa was narrated by Malik from Abu al-Zinad from al-A'raj from Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet. And this indicates the falsehood of the statement of the Qadariyya who say: Indeed Allah, Mighty and Majestic, does not know the thing until it comes to be; because Allah, Mighty and Majestic, if He wrote that and commanded that it be written, then He does not write something He does not know; He is exalted above that and sanctified. And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: {And no leaf falls but that He knows it, nor any grain in the darkness of the earth, nor anything wet or dry, but that it is in a clear Book} (6:59). And He said: {And there is no creature on earth but that upon Allah is its provision, and He knows its dwelling place and its repository} (11:6). And He said: {Allah has encompassed it and they forgot it} (58:6). And He said: {He has counted them and numbered them exactly} (19:94). And He said: {He encompasses everything in knowledge and has counted everything in number} (65:12, 72:28). And He said: {He is Knower of all things} (2:29). So that makes clear that He knows all things. And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has informed that the creation will be raised and gathered, and that the disbelievers will abide eternally in the Fire, and that the prophets and believers will abide eternally in the Gardens, and that the Hour will come, though the Hour has not yet come. So that indicates that Allah, Exalted, knows what will be before it is. And Allah said concerning the people of the Fire: {If they were returned, they would return to what they were forbidden} (6:28); so He informed about what will not be, that if it were, how it would be. And He, Exalted, said: {What is the state of the former generations? He said: Their knowledge is with my Lord in a Book; my Lord does not err nor does He forget} (20:51-52). And whoever does not know the thing before its occurrence does not know after its passing. Exalted is Allah above the saying of the wrongdoers, greatly high.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya sect who claim that Allah does not know events until they occur. The author begins by citing the hadith of Adam and Musa, in which Adam argues with Musa that the sin he committed was written by Allah before the creation of the heavens. The author then states that this hadith demonstrates the falsehood of the Qadariyya, because if Allah writes something and commands it to be written, He must know it; He is far above writing something unknown. Then the author quotes numerous Qur'anic verses to establish Allah's all-encompassing knowledge: the verse from Surah al-An'am that no leaf falls but He knows it; the verse from Surah Hud that every creature's provision and abode are known; the verse from Surah al-Mujadilah that Allah has encompassed them while they forgot; the verse from Surah Maryam that He has counted them exactly; the verse from Surah al-Talaq and al-Jinn that His knowledge surrounds everything and He has counted all things; and the verse from Surah al-Baqarah that He is Knower of all things. These verses show that Allah knows all things. Then the author argues from the fact that Allah has informed us that the creation will be resurrected, that the disbelievers will abide eternally in the Fire, and that the prophets and believers will abide eternally in Paradise, and that the Hour will come even though it has not yet come. This proves that Allah knows what will happen before it happens. Then the author cites the verse about the people of the Fire: 'If they were returned, they would return to what they were forbidden' (6:28) – Allah informed of what they would do if they were returned, which shows His knowledge of what would be. Then the verse from Surah Taha: 'What is the state of the former generations? He said: Their knowledge is with my Lord in a Book; my Lord does not err nor forget' (20:51-52). The author concludes that one who does not know a thing before it occurs cannot know it after it passes. The passage ends with a declaration of Allah's transcendence above the sayings of the wrongdoers.

Key Terms
القدرية
العلم
الكتاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya believed Allah only knows events after they happen.
Correction: The hadith shows Allah wrote the sin before creation, proving He knew it beforehand.

Checkpoint
How does the hadith of Adam and Musa refute the Qadariyya claim?
A) Adam argued that Musa had no right to blame him because the sin was written by Allah before creation, proving Allah knew it beforehand.
B) Musa argued that Adam had no excuse because the sin was not written.
C) The hadith shows that Adam and Musa disputed about predestination, but does not settle the issue.
D) The hadith proves that Allah does not know events until they happen.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of Adam and Musa proves that Allah's knowledge of events is prior to their occurrence because He wrote them before creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Allah wrote every deed of yours before the heavens were created. Does this make you feel hopeless about changing your destiny, or does it fill you with awe at His perfect knowledge? How should this affect the way you approach repentance today?
?
When you sin, do you ever excuse yourself by thinking 'it was written'? How does Adam’s argument with Musa—that he still accepted responsibility despite the writing—challenge that excuse? What will you change in your next moment of weakness?
?
If Allah knows every secret thought you have not yet thought, what does that mean for the hidden parts of your life you prefer to ignore? Will you invite His knowledge to purify them, or continue to pretend they are unseen?

Qur'anic Verses on Allah's All-Encompassing Knowledge
Imam Ash'ari cites six Qur'anic verses to prove that Allah's knowledge is all-encompassing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how multiple Qur'anic verses establish that Allah knows all things, including every leaf, grain, and creature.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge encompasses all things, from the smallest leaf to the largest creation.

After the hadith, Imam Ash'ari marshals a series of Qur'anic verses that explicitly describe the extent of Allah's knowledge. These verses leave no room for the Qadariyya claim that Allah is ignorant of future events. Each verse emphasizes that nothing escapes His knowledge, and that all things are recorded in a clear Book.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses and the conclusion
Read the Arabic passage containing the six verses and the author's concluding statement. Notice the variety of examples: leaf, grain, creatures, counting, etc.
2
Identify the common theme
Each verse emphasizes that Allah knows all things. Look for keywords like 'knows', 'encompasses', 'counts'.
3
Understand the logical implication for the Qadariyya
If Allah knows every leaf and grain, He certainly knows future events. The author concludes that these verses show He knows all things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الَّذِي اصْطَفَاكَ الله بِكَلَامِهِ، تَلُومُنِي عَلَى عَمَلٍ كَتَبَهُ اللهُ عَلَيَّ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ، قَالَ: فَحَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى. وَرُوِيَ حَدِيثُ حَجَّ آدَمُ مُوسَى مَالِكٌ عَنْ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَنِ الأَعْرَجِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ. وَهَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى بُطْلَانِ قَوْلِ الْقَدَرِيَّةِ الَّذِينَ يَقُولُونَ: إِنَّ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ لَا يَعْلَمُ الشَّيْءَ حَتَّى يَكُونَ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ إِذَا كَتَبَ ذَلِكَ وَأَمَرَ بِأَنْ يُكْتَبَ فَلَا يَكْتُبُ شَيْئًا لَا يَعْلَمُهُ، جَلَّ عَنْ ذَلِكَ وَتَقَدَّسَ. وَقَالَ اللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: ﴿وَمَا نَسْقُطُ مِن وَرَقَةٍ إِلَّا يَعْلَمُهَا وَلَا حَبَّةٍ فِي ظُلُمَتِ الْأَرْضِ وَلَا رَطْبٍ وَلَا يَابِسٍ إِلَّا فِي كِتَبٍ مُّبِينٍ﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿وَمَا مِن دَابَّةٍ فِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَّا عَلَى اللهِ رِزْقُهَا وَيَعْلَمُ مُسْتَقَرَّهَا وَمُسْتَوْدَعَهَا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿أَحْصَاهُ اللهُ وَنَسُوهُ﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿لَقَدْ أَحْصَاهُمْ وَعَدَّهُمْ عَدًّا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿أَحَاطَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عِلْمًا وَأَحْصَى كُلَّ شَيْءٍ عَدَدًا﴾ وَقَالَ: ﴿بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ﴾ فَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّهُ يَعْلَمُ الْأَشْيَاءَ كُلَّهَا. وَقَدْ أَخْبَرَ اللهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ أَنَّ الْخَلْقَ يُبْعَثُونَ وَيُحْشَرُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْكَافِرِينَ فِي النَّارِ يُخَلَّدُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْأَنْبِيَاءَ وَالْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي الْجِنَانِ يُخَلَّدُونَ، وَأَنَّ الْقِيَامَةَ تَقُومُ وَلَمْ تَقُمِ الْقِيَامَةُ بَعْدُ، فَذَلِكَ يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى يَعْلَمُ مَا يَكُونَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَكُونَ. وَقَدْ قَالَ اللهُ فِي أَهْلِ النَّارِ: ﴿وَلَوْ رُدُّوا لَعَادُوا لِمَا نُهُوا عَنْهُ﴾ فَأَخْبَرَ عَمَّا لَا يَكُونُ أَنْ لَوْ كَانَ كَيْفَ يَكُونُ. وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَمَا بَالُ الْقُرُونِ الْأُولَى قَالَ عِلْمُهَا عِندَ رَبِّي فِي كِتَبٍ لَّا يَضِلُّ رَبِّي وَلَا يَنسَى﴾ وَمَنْ لَا يَعْلَمُ الشَّيْءَ قَبْلَ كَوْنِهِ لَا يَعْلَمُ بَعْدَ تَقَضِّيهِ، تَعَالَى اللهُ عَنْ قَوْلِ الظَّالِمِينَ عُلُوًّا كَبِيرًا.
He whom Allah chose with His speech, you blame me for a deed that Allah wrote upon me before He created the heavens. He said: So Adam argued with Musa. And the hadith of Adam arguing with Musa was narrated by Malik from Abu al-Zinad from al-A'raj from Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet. And this indicates the falsehood of the statement of the Qadariyya who say: Indeed Allah, Mighty and Majestic, does not know the thing until it comes to be; because Allah, Mighty and Majestic, if He wrote that and commanded that it be written, then He does not write something He does not know; He is exalted above that and sanctified. And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, said: {And no leaf falls but that He knows it, nor any grain in the darkness of the earth, nor anything wet or dry, but that it is in a clear Book} (6:59). And He said: {And there is no creature on earth but that upon Allah is its provision, and He knows its dwelling place and its repository} (11:6). And He said: {Allah has encompassed it and they forgot it} (58:6). And He said: {He has counted them and numbered them exactly} (19:94). And He said: {He encompasses everything in knowledge and has counted everything in number} (65:12, 72:28). And He said: {He is Knower of all things} (2:29). So that makes clear that He knows all things. And Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has informed that the creation will be raised and gathered, and that the disbelievers will abide eternally in the Fire, and that the prophets and believers will abide eternally in the Gardens, and that the Hour will come, though the Hour has not yet come. So that indicates that Allah, Exalted, knows what will be before it is. And Allah said concerning the people of the Fire: {If they were returned, they would return to what they were forbidden} (6:28); so He informed about what will not be, that if it were, how it would be. And He, Exalted, said: {What is the state of the former generations? He said: Their knowledge is with my Lord in a Book; my Lord does not err nor does He forget} (20:51-52). And whoever does not know the thing before its occurrence does not know after its passing. Exalted is Allah above the saying of the wrongdoers, greatly high.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya sect who claim that Allah does not know events until they occur. The author begins by citing the hadith of Adam and Musa, in which Adam argues with Musa that the sin he committed was written by Allah before the creation of the heavens. The author then states that this hadith demonstrates the falsehood of the Qadariyya, because if Allah writes something and commands it to be written, He must know it; He is far above writing something unknown. Then the author quotes numerous Qur'anic verses to establish Allah's all-encompassing knowledge: the verse from Surah al-An'am that no leaf falls but He knows it; the verse from Surah Hud that every creature's provision and abode are known; the verse from Surah al-Mujadilah that Allah has encompassed them while they forgot; the verse from Surah Maryam that He has counted them exactly; the verse from Surah al-Talaq and al-Jinn that His knowledge surrounds everything and He has counted all things; and the verse from Surah al-Baqarah that He is Knower of all things. These verses show that Allah knows all things. Then the author argues from the fact that Allah has informed us that the creation will be resurrected, that the disbelievers will abide eternally in the Fire, and that the prophets and believers will abide eternally in Paradise, and that the Hour will come even though it has not yet come. This proves that Allah knows what will happen before it happens. Then the author cites the verse about the people of the Fire: 'If they were returned, they would return to what they were forbidden' (6:28) – Allah informed of what they would do if they were returned, which shows His knowledge of what would be. Then the verse from Surah Taha: 'What is the state of the former generations? He said: Their knowledge is with my Lord in a Book; my Lord does not err nor forget' (20:51-52). The author concludes that one who does not know a thing before it occurs cannot know it after it passes. The passage ends with a declaration of Allah's transcendence above the sayings of the wrongdoers.

Key Terms
العلم
الكتاب
الإحصاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following verses is NOT cited in this passage?
A) And no leaf falls but that He knows it
B) And there is no creature on earth but that upon Allah is its provision
C) He knows what is in the heavens and the earth
D) He encompasses everything in knowledge

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic verses explicitly state that Allah's knowledge covers every detail of creation, refuting the idea that He is unaware of future events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin in secret, do you truly believe that Allah sees every leaf fall and every grain, and that He knows your hidden action? How would your behavior change if you lived with that certainty every moment?
?
Allah has counted every detail of your life—your breaths, your thoughts, your intentions. Does this comfort you or frighten you? Will you let it lead you to gratitude and repentance, or to heedlessness?
?
If Allah knows the future of every leaf, then He knows your tomorrow, your next year, and your final breath. Are you living as if you believe that, or are you planning your life as if you control it? What needs to change today?
